| ↳ tension_does_zero_work_circular | nano | example |  | T ⊥ v in uniform circular motion. | parent: zero_work_when_F_perpendicular_v |  |  |
| ↳ kinetic_energy_always_positive | nano | ✅ |  | K = ½mv² ≥ 0 always (since v² ≥ 0). | parent: kinetic_energy_definition |  |  |
| ↳ KE_change_only_by_tangential_force | nano | ✅ |  | Only F_t contributes to dK/dt; F_r doesn't. | parent: kinetic_energy_definition |  |  |
| ↳ work_energy_theorem_derivation | nano | ✅ |  | From F = ma, ∫F·dr = ∫m(dv/dt)dr = ∫mv·dv = ½mv² − ½mu². | parent: work_energy_theorem_single_particle |  |  |
| ↳ WET_holds_in_non_inertial_frames_with_pseudo | nano | extension |  | HCV1 Points to Ponder #6 + Q.7. Include pseudo-force work. | parent: work_energy_theorem_single_particle |  |  |
| ↳ internal_force_pair_can_do_net_work | nano | example |  | HCV1 §8.4 + Points to Ponder #3. Two attracting charges: F_AB + F_BA = 0 but W ≠ 0. EPIC-C candidate. | parent: work_energy_theorem_system_of_particles |  |  |
| ↳ round_trip_work_zero_test_for_conservative | nano | test |  | ∮F·dr = 0 ⇔ conservative. | parent: conservative_vs_nonconservative_forces |  |  |
| ↳ gravity_is_conservative | nano | example |  | Round-trip W = 0. | parent: conservative_vs_nonconservative_forces |  |  |

| ↳ friction_is_nonconservative | nano | example |  | Round-trip W = −2μmgd ≠ 0. | parent: conservative_vs_nonconservative_forces |  |  |
| ↳ only_change_in_U_is_defined | nano | clarification |  | Choice of zero is arbitrary. HCV1 §8.7. | parent: potential_energy_definition_general |  |  |

## T14 — Momentum Collisions  *(Class 11)*

*10 atomic + 14 nano = 24 concepts.*

| Concept ID | Type | Sim | Diamond | Description (what it teaches) | Requires | Required-by | Targets misconception |
|---|---|:---:|:---:|---|---|---|---|
| **centre_of_mass_atomic** | atomic | ✅ | 💎 | Mathematical point R = Σmᵢrᵢ/Σmᵢ representing weighted-average position of system; CoM moves as if all mass were concentrated there and all external force acted there | [vector_addition(T5), vector_resolution(T5)] | [linear_momentum_atomic, conservation_of_momentum_atomic] |  |
| ↳ com_discrete_particles_nano | nano | ✅ |  | R = (m₁r₁ + m₂r₂ + ...)/(m₁+m₂+...); for 2-body case R = (m₁r₁ + m₂r₂)/(m₁+m₂); CoM closer to heavier mass | [centre_of_mass_atomic] | [reduced_mass_atomic] |  |
| ↳ com_continuous_body_nano | nano | ✅ |  | R = (∫r dm)/M; integration over body's mass distribution; symmetric body's CoM at geometric centre | [centre_of_mass_atomic, calculus_integration(math-tools)] | — |  |
| ↳ com_motion_v_com_eq_p_total_over_m_nano | nano | ✅ |  | V_CoM = (Σmᵢvᵢ)/M = P_total/M; CoM moves with system's average velocity. **cognitive_error_target:** "CoM is a material point" → CoM is a MATHEMATICAL location, may be outside any actual body | [centre_of_mass_atomic] | [linear_momentum_atomic] |  |
| **linear_momentum_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | p = mv (single body); P_system = Σmᵢvᵢ = M·V_CoM (system); SI units kg·m/s. Momentum is the natural quantity behind Newton's 2nd law (F = dp/dt) | [centre_of_mass_atomic, newton_second_law_atomic(T11)] | [conservation_of_momentum_atomic, impulse_momentum_theorem_nano, kinetic_theory_pressure_atomic(T27)] |  |
| ↳ impulse_momentum_theorem_nano | nano | ✅ |  | J = ∫F dt = Δp; impulse equals change in momentum; cross-link to T11 `impulse_change_in_momentum_nano` | [linear_momentum_atomic, newton_second_law_atomic(T11), calculus_integration(math-tools)] | — |  |
| **conservation_of_momentum_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | When no external force acts on a system (or net external force is zero), total linear momentum is conserved: ΣP_initial = ΣP_final. Follows from Newton's 3rd law applied to internal forces (they cancel pairwise) | [linear_momentum_atomic, newton_third_law_atomic(T11)] | [elastic_collision_1d_atomic, inelastic_collision_atomic, perfectly_inelastic_collision_atomic, rocket_equation_atomic, explosion_as_reverse_collision_nano] | momentum conserved always |
| ↳ closed_system_requirement_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Conservation holds ONLY when net external force is zero. Gravity acting on bouncing ball + earth: SYSTEM is conserved (ball + earth), but ball-alone is NOT. **cognitive_error_target nano**. | [conservation_of_momentum_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ explosion_as_reverse_collision_nano | nano | ✅ |  | One body → multiple fragments; total p conserved; KE INCREASES (internal energy → KE). Time-reversed perfectly-inelastic-collision. ISRO multi-stage rocket = controlled explosion at staging events. | [conservation_of_momentum_atomic, perfectly_inelastic_collision_atomic] | — |  |
| **elastic_collision_1d_atomic** | atomic | ✅ | 💎 | 1D collision conserving BOTH momentum AND kinetic energy. Closed-form solution: v₁' = ((m₁−m₂)v₁ + 2m₂v₂)/(m₁+m₂); v₂' = ((m₂−m₁)v₂ + 2m₁v₁)/(m₁+m₂). Equal-mass case: simple velocity exchange. | [conservation_of_momentum_atomic, work_energy_theorem(T13)] | [elastic_collision_2d_atomic, coefficient_of_restitution_atomic] |  |
| ↳ equal_mass_velocity_exchange_nano | nano | ✅ |  | m₁ = m₂: v₁' = v₂; v₂' = v₁. Classic Newton's cradle / billiards visualization. | [elastic_collision_1d_atomic] | — |  |
| **elastic_collision_2d_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | 2D oblique elastic collision: conservation of momentum applied PER COMPONENT (x and y), plus conservation of KE; results in coupled equations. Geometric significance: post-collision velocity directions form right angle for equal masses | [elastic_collision_1d_atomic, vector_resolution(T5), system_of_linear_equations_2var(math-tools)] | [rutherford_scattering(T47), molecular_collision_nano(T27)] |  |
| ↳ right_angle_for_equal_masses_nano | nano | ✅ |  | When equal masses collide elastically with one at rest: post-collision velocity vectors are perpendicular. Classic billiards-shot geometry. | [elastic_collision_2d_atomic] | — |  |
| **inelastic_collision_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | Momentum conserved; KE NOT conserved (some converted to heat, sound, deformation). Coefficient of restitution e ∈ [0,1] characterises energy retention | [conservation_of_momentum_atomic] | [perfectly_inelastic_collision_atomic, real_world_collisions_nano, coefficient_of_restitution_atomic] | real collisions are elastic |
| **perfectly_inelastic_collision_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | Bodies stick together after collision; common post-collision velocity v_f = (m₁v₁ + m₂v₂)/(m₁+m₂); maximum KE-loss case; e = 0 | [inelastic_collision_atomic, conservation_of_momentum_atomic] | [explosion_as_reverse_collision_nano(reverse)] |  |
| ↳ railway_buffer_collision_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Two Indian Railways wagons couple on track: bodies stick (Janney coupler engagement) → perfectly inelastic; coupling-and-uncoupling at Mughalsarai/Bandra/Itarsi yards. | [perfectly_inelastic_collision_atomic] | — |  |
| **coefficient_of_restitution_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | e = \|v_separation\|/\|v_approach\|; e = 1 elastic, e = 0 perfectly inelastic, 0 < e < 1 general inelastic. Property of the COLLISION PAIR (not single object) | [elastic_collision_1d_atomic, inelastic_collision_atomic] | [bouncing_ball_height_nano, cricket_bat_ball_nano] | e is property of one ball |
| ↳ bouncing_ball_height_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Ball dropped from height h₀ bounces to h₁ = e²h₀; nth bounce → h_n = e^(2n)h₀; series of decreasing heights | [coefficient_of_restitution_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ cricket_bat_ball_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Cricket ball-bat collision: e ≈ 0.45 for hardened-leather + willow; affects six-vs-four trajectory; depends on bat-thickness, ball-condition, swing-speed. Indian cricket-equipment-industry context. | [coefficient_of_restitution_atomic] | — |  |
| **rocket_equation_atomic** | atomic | ✅ | 💎 | Tsiolkovsky: v − v₀ = u·ln(M₀/M); rocket gains speed by ejecting mass at exhaust-speed u; specific impulse I_sp = u/g₀ measures fuel efficiency | [conservation_of_momentum_atomic, f_eq_dp_dt_nano(T11), calculus_integration(math-tools), natural_log(math-tools)] | — |  |
| ↳ isro_pslv_multistage_nano | nano | ✅ |  | PSLV: 4 stages (PS1 solid + PS2 liquid + PS3 solid + PS4 liquid); each stage burns + separates (explosion → reverse collision). Total Δv achievable via Tsiolkovsky summed across stages. | [rocket_equation_atomic, explosion_as_reverse_collision_nano] | — |  |
| ↳ specific_impulse_i_sp_nano | nano | — |  | I_sp = u/g₀ in seconds; chemical rocket: 250-450 s; ion thruster: 1000-5000 s; ISRO LAM (liquid apogee motor) ~300 s | [rocket_equation_atomic] | — |  |
| **reduced_mass_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | μ = m₁m₂/(m₁+m₂); converts 2-body problem to equivalent 1-body problem of mass μ moving in central potential. Foundation of 2-body collision + Rutherford scattering + Bohr H-atom correction | [centre_of_mass_atomic, com_discrete_particles_nano] | [rutherford_scattering(T47), bohr_model_reduced_mass_correction(T47)] |  |
| ↳ rutherford_scattering_application_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Alpha + gold-nucleus: μ ≈ m_α since m_Au >> m_α; cross-link to T47 atomic-models | [reduced_mass_atomic, elastic_collision_2d_atomic, rutherford_scattering(T47)] | — |  |

## T15 — Rotational Mechanics  *(Class 11)*

*12 atomic + 15 nano = 27 concepts.*

| Concept ID | Type | Sim | Diamond | Description (what it teaches) | Requires | Required-by | Targets misconception |
|---|---|:---:|:---:|---|---|---|---|
| **rigid_body_rotation_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | Rigid body = all internal distances constant; rotation about fixed axis = every point traces a circle of fixed radius around axis | [vector_resolution(T5)] | [rotational_kinematics_atomic, moment_of_inertia_atomic, torque_atomic] |  |
| ↳ rotation_axis_vs_translation_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Pure rotation = points trace circles around fixed axis (axis is stationary). Pure translation = all points have same velocity. General motion = translation + rotation about CoM | [rigid_body_rotation_atomic, centre_of_mass_atomic(T14)] | — |  |
| **rotational_kinematics_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | ω = dθ/dt; α = dω/dt; ω = ω₀ + αt; θ = ω₀t + ½αt²; ω² = ω₀² + 2αθ. **Rotational analog of T6 linear kinematics.** | [rigid_body_rotation_atomic, calculus_derivative(math-tools)] | [tau_eq_i_alpha_atomic, rolling_on_incline_atomic] | angular and linear kinematics are different physics |
| ↳ omega_v_eq_omega_r_relation_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Linear velocity of point at radius r: v = ωr. Linear acceleration tangential: a_t = αr. Linear acceleration centripetal: a_c = ω²r. **Three relations bridging linear ↔ angular.** | [rotational_kinematics_atomic, circular_motion(T10)] | — |  |
| **moment_of_inertia_atomic** | atomic | ✅ | 💎 | I = Σmᵢrᵢ² (discrete); I = ∫r² dm (continuous). I is "rotational mass" — resists change in rotational motion. **DEPENDS ON CHOSEN AXIS.** | [rigid_body_rotation_atomic, calculus_integration(math-tools)] | [tau_eq_i_alpha_atomic, rotational_work_energy_atomic, angular_momentum_atomic] | I is a property of body alone |
| ↳ i_for_canonical_bodies_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Solid sphere: I = (2/5)MR². Hollow sphere: (2/3)MR². Disc/cylinder about axis: ½MR². Ring: MR². Rod about end: ML²/3. Rod about centre: ML²/12. **Table for V1 reference.** | [moment_of_inertia_atomic] | [rolling_on_incline_atomic] |  |
| ↳ parallel_axis_theorem_nano | nano | ✅ |  | I_parallel = I_CoM + Md²; moment of inertia about any axis parallel to CoM-axis equals I_CoM + (mass × distance²). Allows computing I about arbitrary axis. | [moment_of_inertia_atomic, centre_of_mass_atomic(T14)] | — |  |
| ↳ perpendicular_axis_theorem_nano | nano | ✅ |  | For PLANAR body in xy-plane: I_z = I_x + I_y. Only valid for thin laminar (planar) bodies; not for 3D solids. **cognitive_error_target:** "perpendicular-axis applies to all bodies" → planar only. | [moment_of_inertia_atomic] | — |  |
| **torque_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | τ = r × F (vector form); τ = rF sin θ (magnitude); τ is to angular motion what F is to linear motion. SI unit: N·m | [rigid_body_rotation_atomic, vector_cross_product(math-tools), newton_second_law_atomic(T11)] | [tau_eq_i_alpha_atomic, angular_momentum_atomic, conservation_of_angular_momentum_atomic] |  |
| ↳ moment_arm_lever_arm_nano | nano | ✅ |  | τ = F × d_perpendicular = F × (r sin θ). Moment arm = perpendicular distance from axis to line-of-action of force. **cognitive_error_target:** "torque = r·F always" → r sin θ matters; force ALONG r contributes ZERO torque | [torque_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ couples_two_equal_opposite_forces_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Pair of equal-opposite forces with separation d: net force = 0; net torque = F·d (independent of axis choice). Door-handle, wrench-on-bolt examples | [torque_atomic] | — |  |
| **tau_eq_i_alpha_atomic** | atomic | ✅ | 💎 | τ_net = Iα; central quantitative law of rotational dynamics. Rotational analog of F_net = ma | [torque_atomic, moment_of_inertia_atomic, rotational_kinematics_atomic, newton_second_law_atomic(T11)] | [rolling_on_incline_atomic, torsional_pendulum_atomic, rotational_work_energy_atomic] |  |
| ↳ rotational_vs_linear_table_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Side-by-side table: m↔I, F↔τ, v↔ω, a↔α, F=ma↔τ=Iα, p=mv↔L=Iω, KE=½mv²↔KE=½Iω². **Cognitive scaffold nano.** | [tau_eq_i_alpha_atomic] | — |  |
| **rotational_work_energy_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | W_torque = ∫τ dθ; rotational KE = ½Iω²; total KE for rolling = ½mv² + ½Iω². Bridges T13 Work-Energy linear treatment | [tau_eq_i_alpha_atomic, work_energy_theorem(T13)] | [rolling_on_incline_atomic, pure_rolling_atomic] |  |
| **angular_momentum_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | L = Iω (rotational) = r × p (general); SI unit: kg·m²/s; vector quantity; direction by right-hand rule along ω | [torque_atomic, moment_of_inertia_atomic, rotational_kinematics_atomic] | [conservation_of_angular_momentum_atomic, torsional_pendulum_atomic, magnetic_dipole_moment(T36)] | L is a scalar |
| ↳ l_eq_r_cross_p_nano | nano | ✅ |  | For a single particle: L = r × p; for system: L_total = Σ(rᵢ × pᵢ); axis-independent definition | [angular_momentum_atomic, vector_cross_product(math-tools)] | — |  |
| **conservation_of_angular_momentum_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | When no external torque acts (τ_ext = 0): L_total = constant. Derivation: τ_ext = dL/dt = 0 → L = const. **Pirouette, planetary Kepler-2, gyroscope-stability all apply** | [angular_momentum_atomic, torque_atomic] | [pirouette_application_nano, keplers_2nd_law_application_nano(T16)] |  |
| ↳ pirouette_application_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Ice-skater / Bharatnatyam dancer pirouette: arms pulled in → I decreases → ω increases (L = Iω constant). Indian classical-dance everyday observation | [conservation_of_angular_momentum_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ isro_satellite_attitude_control_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Geostationary satellites use reaction-wheel-based attitude control: spinning wheel inside satellite changes satellite's angular momentum; ISRO INSAT/GSAT/Cartosat all use this | [conservation_of_angular_momentum_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ keplers_2nd_law_planetary_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Law of equal areas: planets sweep equal areas in equal times → dA/dt = L/2m = constant (when L conserved under central force). Cross-link to T16 Gravitation | [conservation_of_angular_momentum_atomic, gravitation(T16)] | — |  |
| **pure_rolling_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | Rolling without slipping: v_CoM = Rω (constraint); contact-point velocity = 0 instantaneously; STATIC friction (not kinetic) provides the rotational coupling | [rotational_kinematics_atomic, omega_v_eq_omega_r_relation_nano, friction_force_atomic(T11), centre_of_mass_atomic(T14)] | [rolling_on_incline_atomic, total_ke_rolling_nano] | rolling friction is kinetic |
| ↳ contact_point_instantaneous_rest_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Rolling-without-slipping condition: v_CoM − Rω = 0 → contact point has zero velocity at any instant. **Diamond visualisation candidate**: trace path of contact point = cycloid | [pure_rolling_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ total_ke_rolling_nano | nano | ✅ |  | KE_total = KE_translation + KE_rotation = ½mv_CoM² + ½Iω² = ½mv² + ½I(v/R)² = ½v²(m + I/R²). Larger I/R² → more KE in rotation | [pure_rolling_atomic, rotational_work_energy_atomic] | — |  |
| **rolling_on_incline_atomic** | atomic | ✅ | 💎 | Body rolling without slipping down incline angle θ: a_CoM = g sin θ / (1 + I/(mR²)); time-to-bottom depends on I/(mR²) ratio. **Solid sphere < disc < hollow sphere < ring** | [pure_rolling_atomic, tau_eq_i_alpha_atomic, block_on_incline_atomic(T11), i_for_canonical_bodies_nano] | — |  |
| ↳ rolling_race_demonstration_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Race down same incline: solid sphere wins (smallest I/mR² = 2/5); disc 2nd (1/2); hollow sphere 3rd (2/3); ring last (1.0). Iconic Class 11 demo | [rolling_on_incline_atomic, i_for_canonical_bodies_nano] | — |  |
| **torsional_pendulum_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | Disc suspended by wire with torsional rigidity κ: τ = −κθ → I·d²θ/dt² = −κθ → angular SHM with ω² = κ/I; T = 2π√(I/κ) | [tau_eq_i_alpha_atomic, simple_harmonic_motion(T17), angular_shm_equation(T17)] | — |  |
| **flywheel_application_atomic** | atomic | ✅ | 💎 | Wheel with large I stores rotational KE = ½Iω² and smooths angular-velocity fluctuations. Automotive engine flywheel, power-plant turbine inertia, KERS (Kinetic Energy Recovery System) all use this | [moment_of_inertia_atomic, rotational_work_energy_atomic] | — |  |

*28 atomic + 28 nano = 56 concepts.*

| Concept ID | Type | Sim | Diamond | Description (what it teaches) | Requires | Required-by | Targets misconception |
|---|---|:---:|:---:|---|---|---|---|
| **newton_law_of_gravitation** | atomic | ✅ | 💎 | `F = Gm₁m₂/r²`, central + conservative + medium-independent. The diamond seed. | [vector_resolution, inverse_square_concept_from_T30] | [acceleration_due_to_gravity, gravitational_field_strength, gravitational_PE_general] |  |
| ↳ force_between_two_point_masses | nano | ✅ |  | DCM2 Fig 13.1 | [newton_law_of_gravitation] | [newton_law_of_gravitation] |  |
| ↳ force_between_two_spherical_bodies | nano | ✅ |  | DCM2 Fig 13.2; shell theorem makes this identical to point-mass | [newton_law_of_gravitation, shell_theorem_external] | [newton_law_of_gravitation] |  |
| ↳ force_between_sphere_and_rod_integration | nano | ✅ |  | DCM2 Fig 13.4 + Example 13.5; ∫dF over rod length | [newton_law_of_gravitation, integration_basics] | [newton_law_of_gravitation] |  |
| ↳ superposition_polygon_vertex_masses | nano | ✅ |  | DCM2 Examples 13.2/13.3/13.4 hexagon/pentagon/square | [newton_law_of_gravitation, vector_resolution] | [newton_law_of_gravitation] |  |

| ↳ small_angle_sin_theta_approx_theta | nano | ✅ |  | sin θ ≈ θ for θ < 0.349 rad (20°). Justifies linearization. | ↳ pendulum_independent_of_mass_and_amplitude | nano | ✅ |  | T does not depend on bob mass or (small) amplitude — the Galileo observation. Per NCERT 14.8.2 introductory paragraph. | simple_pendulum_period_formula | — |  |
| **g_determination_via_pendulum_in_lab** | atomic | ✅ |  | g = 4π²L/T². Lab procedure: measure 20 oscillations to reduce stopwatch error. HCV1 §12.8 (Determination of g). | simple_pendulum_period_formula | — |  |
| **physical_pendulum_period_formula** | atomic | ✅ |  | Per S-G4. Rigid body suspended through point O: T = 2π√(I/mgL). HCV1 §12.9. Rod-as-pendulum, meter-stick-pendulum patterns. | simple_pendulum_period_formula, moment_of_inertia_atomic [T16] | — |  |
| **angular_shm_equation_gamma_minus_k_theta** | atomic | ✅ |  | Per S-G5. Angular equivalent of F=−kx: Γ = −kθ. T = 2π√(I/k). HCV1 §12.7. **Indian-context anchor:** hanging umbrella oscillations. | shm_definition_force_minus_kx, physical_pendulum_period_formula, moment_of_inertia_atomic [T16] | torsional_pendulum_disc_on_wire_period, T30:A38 (dipole as ang SHM) |  |
| ↳ angular_omega_squared_equals_k_over_I | nano | ✅ |  | ω² = k/I. Analogous to k/m in linear SHM. | angular_shm_equation_gamma_minus_k_theta | — |  |
| **torsional_pendulum_disc_on_wire_period** | atomic | ✅ |  | Disc twisted on wire: torsional constant k, T = 2π√(I/k). HCV1 §12.10 (Fig 12.14). Used for measuring torsional rigidity. | angular_shm_equation_gamma_minus_k_theta, moment_of_inertia_atomic [T16] | — |  |
| **damping_force_proportional_to_velocity** | atomic | ✅ |  | F_d = −bv. Total force on block: m d²x/dt² + b dx/dt + kx = 0. NCERT §14.9. | shm_definition_force_minus_kx, viscous_drag [T16] | damped_oscillation_solution_exp_decay_envelope, forced_oscillation_steady_state_at_driver_frequency |  |
| ↳ b_dimensionless_ratio_b_over_sqrt_km | nano | ✅ |  | b/√(km) determines damping regime. NCERT Eq 14.34 onward. | damping_force_proportional_to_velocity | damped_oscillation_solution_exp_decay_envelope |  |
| **damped_oscillation_solution_exp_decay_envelope** | atomic | ✅ |  | x(t) = A e^(−bt/2m) cos(ω′t + φ), ω′ = √(k/m − b²/4m²). Amplitude decays exponentially. NCERT Fig 14.20. | damping_force_proportional_to_velocity | forced_oscillation_steady_state_at_driver_frequency |  |
| ↳ t_half_amplitude_decay | nano | ✅ |  | T_{1/2,amp} = (ln 2)·2m/b. From e^(−bt/2m) = 1/2. NCERT Ex 14.10. | damped_oscillation_solution_exp_decay_envelope | — |  |
| ↳ t_half_energy_is_half_of_amplitude_half | nano | ✅ |  | E ∝ A² → T_{1/2,energy} = T_{1/2,amp}/2. Common JEE distinction. NCERT Ex 14.10(c). | damped_oscillation_solution_exp_decay_envelope | — |  |
| ↳ critical_damping_concept | nano | ✅ |  | When b²/4m² = k/m, motion just barely returns without oscillating. HCV1 §12.12. | damping_force_proportional_to_velocity | — |  |
| **forced_oscillation_steady_state_at_driver_frequency** | atomic | ✅ |  | External F₀ cos(ω_d t) drives system. Eventually x(t) = A_d cos(ω_d t + φ), at driver frequency ω_d, not natural ω. NCERT §14.10. | damping_force_proportional_to_velocity, damped_oscillation_solution_exp_decay_envelope | resonance_amplitude_peaks_at_natural_frequency |  |
| **resonance_amplitude_peaks_at_natural_frequency** | atomic | ✅ |  | Amplitude A_d maximum when ω_d ≈ ω. Peak sharpness ↑ when damping ↓. NCERT Fig 14.21. **Indian-context anchor:** "Soldiers go out of step while crossing a bridge — same reason an earthquake will not cause uniform damage to all buildings, even of same strength" (direct NCERT 14.10 closing paragraph). | forced_oscillation_steady_state_at_driver_frequency | — |  |
| ↳ coupled_pendulum_demonstration_natural_freq_match | nano | ✅ |  | 5 pendulums on common rope: only the one with matching length picks up large amplitude. NCERT Fig 14.22. | resonance_amplitude_peaks_at_natural_frequency | — |  |
| **linear_combination_of_sin_and_cos_is_shm** | atomic | ✅ |  | A sin ωt + B cos ωt = D sin(ωt + φ) where D = √(A²+B²), tan φ = B/A. The trig-identity bedrock. NCERT Eq 14.3c, HCV1 §12.11. | shm_displacement_xt_sinusoidal | superposition_two_shm_same_direction, perpendicular_two_shm_lissajous_figures |  |
| **superposition_two_shm_same_direction** | atomic | ✅ |  | Per S-G6 split (A). Two SHMs along same axis with phase difference δ: x = A sin(ωt + ε) where A = √(A₁²+A₂²+2A₁A₂ cos δ). HCV1 §12.11(A). | shm_displacement_xt_sinusoidal, linear_combination_of_sin_and_cos_is_shm | — |  |
| ↳ delta_equals_zero_amplitudes_add_constructive | nano | ✅ |  | δ=0: A = A₁ + A₂. Constructive. | superposition_two_shm_same_direction | — |  |
| ↳ delta_equals_pi_amplitudes_subtract_destructive | nano | ✅ |  | δ=π: A = \\|A₁ − A₂\\|. Destructive. Zero amplitude if A₁=A₂. | superposition_two_shm_same_direction | — |  |
| ↳ vector_method_phasor_addition | nano | ✅ |  | Represent each SHM as a vector of magnitude A_i at angle δ_i. Resultant by parallelogram. HCV1 §12.11 Vector Method, Fig 12.16. | superposition_two_shm_same_direction | perpendicular_two_shm_lissajous_figures |  |
| **perpendicular_two_shm_lissajous_figures** | atomic | ✅ |  | Per S-G6 split (B). Two SHMs along perpendicular axes (x and y). General path is ellipse: x²/A₁² + y²/A₂² − 2xy cos δ/(A₁A₂) = sin²δ. HCV1 §12.11(B). | shm_displacement_xt_sinusoidal, shm_as_projection_of_uniform_circular_motion | — |  |
| ↳ delta_zero_line_through_origin_positive_slope | nano | ✅ |  | δ=0: y = (A₂/A₁) x. Line through origin, slope +A₂/A₁. Fig 12.19. | perpendicular_two_shm_lissajous_figures | — |  |
| ↳ delta_pi_line_through_origin_negative_slope | nano | ✅ |  | δ=π: y = −(A₂/A₁) x. Line, negative slope. Fig 12.20. | perpendicular_two_shm_lissajous_figures | — |  |
| ↳ delta_pi_over_2_ellipse_along_axes | nano | ✅ |  | δ=π/2: x²/A₁² + y²/A₂² = 1. Standard ellipse along the coordinate axes. Fig 12.21. | perpendicular_two_shm_lissajous_figures | — |  |
| ↳ equal_amplitudes_delta_pi_over_2_circle | nano | ✅ |  | A₁=A₂ AND δ=π/2: x²+y² = A². Pure circle. (Foreshadow of UCM→SHM bridge.) | perpendicular_two_shm_lissajous_figures | — |  |

## T18 — Elasticity  *(Class 11)*

*10 atomic + 14 nano = 24 concepts.*

| Concept ID | Type | Sim | Diamond | Description (what it teaches) | Requires | Required-by | Targets misconception |
|---|---|:---:|:---:|---|---|---|---|
| **rigid_body_idealisation_breaks_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | Rigid-body assumption (T11-T17) is an idealisation; real bodies deform under applied forces; elasticity is the theory of small-deformation regime | [newton_second_law_atomic(T11)] | [stress_strain_atomic, hookes_law_atomic] |  |
| **stress_strain_atomic** | atomic | ✅ | 💎 | Stress = F/A (force per unit area; SI: Pa = N/m²). Strain = ΔL/L (dimensionless ratio of deformation to original dimension). **Three stress types: tensile (axial), shear (tangential), hydraulic (uniform pressure)**. | [rigid_body_idealisation_breaks_atomic, newton_second_law_atomic(T11)] | [hookes_law_atomic, youngs_modulus_atomic, modulus_of_rigidity_atomic, bulk_modulus_atomic] |  |
| ↳ tensile_compressive_stress_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Force F along axis: F/A acts along normal. Tensile = pulling apart; compressive = pushing together. Same magnitude/formula, opposite directions. | [stress_strain_atomic] | [youngs_modulus_atomic] |  |
| ↳ shear_stress_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Force F tangential to surface area A: F/A acts in plane. Pure shear deforms a rectangle into a parallelogram. Cross-link to T15 torque (rotational analog). | [stress_strain_atomic] | [modulus_of_rigidity_atomic] |  |
| ↳ hydraulic_volumetric_stress_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Uniform pressure P acts on all surfaces of body: volumetric stress = P (SI: Pa). Strain = ΔV/V. Applies in deep oceans, hydraulic presses, atmospheric compression. | [stress_strain_atomic] | [bulk_modulus_atomic] |  |
| **hookes_law_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | Within elastic limit: stress ∝ strain → stress = E × strain (where E is the relevant modulus). Linear regime only. | [stress_strain_atomic] | [youngs_modulus_atomic, modulus_of_rigidity_atomic, bulk_modulus_atomic, stress_strain_curve_atomic] | Hooke's law applies always |
| **stress_strain_curve_atomic** | atomic | ✅ | 💎 | Graphical representation showing: proportional limit (Hooke's law) → elastic limit → yield point → plastic regime → ultimate stress → fracture. Different materials show distinct curves (steel: brittle; rubber: ultra-elastic; glass: brittle no-yield) | [stress_strain_atomic, hookes_law_atomic] | [elastic_pe_atomic] |  |
| ↳ proportional_vs_elastic_vs_plastic_regimes_nano | nano | ✅ |  | (1) Proportional limit: Hooke holds. (2) Elastic limit: deformation reverses on unloading; non-linear in this band. (3) Yield point: plastic deformation begins. (4) Plastic regime: permanent deformation. (5) Ultimate stress: peak before fracture. **Cognitive scaffold nano.** | [stress_strain_curve_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ ductile_vs_brittle_materials_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Ductile (large plastic regime): copper, aluminum, gold — drawn into wire. Brittle (negligible plastic regime): glass, cast iron — shatter without warning. Indian materials industry context. | [stress_strain_curve_atomic] | — |  |
| **youngs_modulus_atomic** | atomic | ✅ | 💎 | Y = (F/A) / (ΔL/L) = stress / longitudinal strain; characterises tensile/compressive deformation. **Industrial values:** steel ~200 GPa, aluminum ~70 GPa, brass ~91 GPa, rubber ~0.01-0.1 GPa | [stress_strain_atomic, hookes_law_atomic, tensile_compressive_stress_nano] | [elastic_pe_atomic, wave_speed_string(T21)] | Y depends on size of body |
| ↳ steel_vs_aluminum_vs_rubber_y_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Steel Y ≈ 200 GPa (high stiffness; structural). Aluminum Y ≈ 70 GPa (lighter; aerospace). Rubber Y ≈ 0.01-0.1 GPa (extremely flexible; tires + seals). **Materials-selection table.** | [youngs_modulus_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ tata_steel_rail_track_y_application_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Indian Railways rail tracks: high-carbon-steel Y ≈ 210 GPa; spec'd to specific elongation under thermal expansion + dynamic load. Tata Steel + SAIL manufacture per IR specs. | [youngs_modulus_atomic, steel_vs_aluminum_vs_rubber_y_nano] | — |  |
| **modulus_of_rigidity_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | η = (F/A) / (Δx/L) = shear stress / shear strain; characterises shear deformation. Typically 0.3-0.5 × Y for metals | [stress_strain_atomic, hookes_law_atomic, shear_stress_nano] | [torsional_pendulum_atomic(T15)] |  |
| ↳ torsion_of_wire_application_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Torsion of cylindrical wire by torque τ: angle of twist φ = τL / (η · I_polar); used in torsional pendulum + torsion balance (Cavendish experiment for G measurement) | [modulus_of_rigidity_atomic, torsional_pendulum_atomic(T15)] | — |  |
| **bulk_modulus_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | K = −V(dP/dV) = −(volumetric stress) / (volumetric strain). Negative sign because volume DECREASES as pressure INCREASES. Compressibility = 1/K | [stress_strain_atomic, hookes_law_atomic, hydraulic_volumetric_stress_nano] | — |  |
| ↳ k_for_solids_liquids_gases_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Solids: K ~10^11 Pa (steel ~160 GPa). Liquids: K ~10^9 Pa (water ~2.2 GPa). Gases: K varies with process; ideal gas isothermal K = P; adiabatic K = γP. **Cross-cluster bridge to T27 (ideal gas K = P)** | [bulk_modulus_atomic, ideal_gas_equation(T27)] | — |  |
| ↳ deep_ocean_pressure_application_nano | nano | — |  | Indian Navy submarines (INS Arihant + INS Kalvari) operate at depths ~200-400 m with hydrostatic pressure ~20-40 bar; hull design uses bulk modulus to predict deformation | [bulk_modulus_atomic] | — |  |
| **poissons_ratio_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | σ = −(transverse strain) / (longitudinal strain). When body stretched longitudinally, transverse dimensions shrink slightly. Dimensionless; typical values 0.2-0.5 | [stress_strain_atomic, youngs_modulus_atomic] | — | Poisson's ratio = 0.5 always |
| ↳ poisson_ratio_table_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Cork ≈ 0 (no transverse change). Steel ≈ 0.30. Brass ≈ 0.34. Aluminum ≈ 0.33. Rubber ≈ 0.50 (incompressible volume). Glass ≈ 0.21. | [poissons_ratio_atomic] | — |  |
| **elastic_pe_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | Energy stored in deformed body within elastic limit: U = ½ × stress × strain × volume = ½ × (F/A) × (ΔL/L) × A·L = ½·F·ΔL. Bridges to T17 SHM spring elastic-PE (½kx²) and T13 Work-Energy general | [stress_strain_atomic, hookes_law_atomic, work_energy_theorem(T13)] | — |  |
| ↳ spring_energy_half_kx_squared_bridge_nano | nano | ✅ |  | For spring (Hooke's-law system): U = ½kx². Identical form to ½·stress·strain·V because spring IS a Hooke's-law system with effective E·A/L = k | [elastic_pe_atomic, spring_force_atomic(T11)] | — |  |
| **construction_engineering_applications_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | Beam loading, cantilever bending, bridge engineering all use elasticity: deflection ∝ load/Y; safety factor = ultimate stress / working stress. **Indian civil engineering context** | [youngs_modulus_atomic, modulus_of_rigidity_atomic, stress_strain_curve_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ l_t_construction_bridge_y_application_nano | nano | — |  | L&T Construction (Mumbai Sea Link, Bandra-Worli, Bogibeel Bridge): structural-steel Y critical for deflection prediction; safety factor 2-3× ultimate stress | [construction_engineering_applications_atomic, youngs_modulus_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ drdo_armor_composite_y_application_nano | nano | — |  | DRDO + Indian armed forces armor: composites with high Y per unit weight; ceramic-metal-polymer combinations; Arjun tank + Tejas LCA airframe applications | [construction_engineering_applications_atomic, youngs_modulus_atomic] | — |  |

## T19 — Wave Equation  *(Class 11)*

*8 atomic + 15 nano = 23 concepts.*

| Concept ID | Type | Sim | Diamond | Description (what it teaches) | Requires | Required-by | Targets misconception |
|---|---|:---:|:---:|---|---|---|---|
| **transverse_vs_longitudinal_atomic** | atomic | ✅ | 💎 | Wave = propagating disturbance. **Transverse:** particle displacement ⊥ to propagation (string, light, water surface). **Longitudinal:** particle displacement ∥ to propagation (sound, pressure). All waves transport energy + momentum WITHOUT net mass transfer. | [shm_atomic(T17)] | [travelling_wave_function_atomic, wave_speed_string_atomic] |  |
| ↳ string_wave_demo_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Transverse: shake one end of long string → pulse travels along string while each particle moves up-down only. Classroom demo + lab. | [transverse_vs_longitudinal_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ slinky_longitudinal_demo_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Slinky compression-rarefaction = longitudinal wave demo; Indian classroom physics-lab standard. | [transverse_vs_longitudinal_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ water_surface_mixed_wave_nano | nano | — |  | Surface water waves: particles trace small circles → mixed transverse + longitudinal. Indian coastal observation (Marina Beach, Goa). | [transverse_vs_longitudinal_atomic] | — |  |
| **travelling_wave_function_atomic** | atomic | ✅ | 💎 | Sinusoidal travelling wave: y(x, t) = A sin(kx − ωt + φ). Right-moving: argument (kx − ωt). Left-moving: (kx + ωt). Phase velocity v = ω/k. | [transverse_vs_longitudinal_atomic, shm_atomic(T17)] | [wave_equation_pde_atomic, wave_parameters_atomic, particle_vs_wave_velocity_atomic] | particles travel with wave |
| ↳ pulse_vs_continuous_wave_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Pulse = single disturbance (e.g., one shake of string). Continuous wave = repeated sinusoidal source. Both obey wave equation; pulse = sum-of-sinusoids via Fourier (bridge to T22). | [travelling_wave_function_atomic] | — |  |
| **wave_parameters_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | Wave parameters: amplitude A, wavelength λ, period T, frequency f = 1/T, angular frequency ω = 2πf, wave-number k = 2π/λ. Universal relation v = fλ = ω/k. | [travelling_wave_function_atomic, shm_atomic(T17)] | [wave_speed_string_atomic, wave_energy_power_atomic] |  |
| ↳ amplitude_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Maximum displacement from equilibrium. Units: m (transverse) or m (longitudinal displacement) or Pa (sound pressure amplitude). | [wave_parameters_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ wavelength_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Spatial period: distance between consecutive crests (or any 2π phase-matched points). λ = v/f. | [wave_parameters_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ period_frequency_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Temporal period T = time for one full cycle; f = 1/T = cycles/sec. Hz = s⁻¹. | [wave_parameters_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ wavenumber_angular_frequency_nano | nano | ✅ |  | k = 2π/λ (rad/m); ω = 2π/T (rad/s). Both phase-rate quantities; central to wave-equation. | [wave_parameters_atomic] | — |  |
| **wave_equation_pde_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | Second-order PDE: ∂²y/∂t² = v²·∂²y/∂x². Travelling wave y(x±vt) is general solution (d'Alembert). **Linear PDE → superposition holds (foundation for T22).** | [travelling_wave_function_atomic, partial_derivative(math-tools)] | [superposition_principle(T22), maxwell_em_wave(T38)] |  |
| ↳ verification_sub_into_pde_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Substitute y = A sin(kx − ωt) into PDE → ω² = v²k² → v = ω/k. Cognitive scaffold for derivation. | [wave_equation_pde_atomic] | — |  |
| **wave_speed_string_atomic** | atomic | ✅ | 💎 | Speed of transverse wave on stretched string: v = √(T/μ); T = tension (N), μ = linear mass density (kg/m). Derived from Newton's 2nd law on small arc. **Industry-anchored: sitar/tabla/guitar string tuning, Indian Railways rail-vibration diagnostics.** | [travelling_wave_function_atomic, newton_second_law_atomic(T11), wave_parameters_atomic] | [musical_string_tuning_application_nano, rail_vibration_application_nano] |  |
| ↳ musical_string_tuning_application_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Sitar, tabla, sarod, guitar tuning: increase tension T → higher v → higher f (for fixed L). Indian classical music + Western. **Healthcare bridge:** ultrasound transducers also use string-resonance principles. | [wave_speed_string_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ rail_vibration_application_nano | nano | — |  | Indian Railways uses ultrasonic rail-flaw detection: travelling-wave reflections reveal internal cracks. Tata Steel + IR Research Designs & Standards Organisation (RDSO Lucknow) maintain testing standards. | [wave_speed_string_atomic, reflection_at_boundary_atomic] | — |  |
| **particle_vs_wave_velocity_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | v_particle = ∂y/∂t = −Aω cos(kx − ωt) — oscillates ±Aω. v_wave = ω/k — constant phase-velocity. **Two fundamentally different quantities; common JEE confusion.** | [travelling_wave_function_atomic, calculus_partial_derivative(math-tools)] | [wave_energy_power_atomic] | v_particle = v_wave |
| ↳ phase_velocity_vs_group_velocity_nano | nano | — |  | For non-dispersive medium: v_phase = v_group. For dispersive (e.g., deep water, glass-prism light): v_group can differ → wave packet envelope moves at v_group. **V2 extension; flagged.** | [particle_vs_wave_velocity_atomic] | — |  |
| **wave_energy_power_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | Power transmitted: P = ½μvω²A². Energy density ∝ A²f². Bridges T13 Work-Energy (energy transported through fluid/string) + T17 SHM elastic-PE. | [wave_parameters_atomic, particle_vs_wave_velocity_atomic, work_energy_theorem(T13), shm_atomic(T17)] | — |  |
| ↳ intensity_a_squared_dependence_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Wave intensity I = P/A ∝ A²ω² → doubling amplitude quadruples intensity. Critical to T23 sound (dB scale) + T44 wave optics (Malus law variation). | [wave_energy_power_atomic] | — |  |
| **reflection_at_boundary_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | Wave at boundary: **fixed end** → π phase change (crest reflects as trough). **Free end** → 0 phase change. Boundary impedance determines partial reflection + transmission. **Sets up T22 standing waves.** | [travelling_wave_function_atomic, wave_speed_string_atomic] | [standing_waves_atomic(T22), rail_vibration_application_nano] | phase change always at reflection |
| ↳ light_vs_heavy_string_partial_reflection_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Wave on light string hitting junction with heavy string: partial reflection (phase-inverted) + partial transmission (in-phase). Classroom demo. | [reflection_at_boundary_atomic, wave_speed_string_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ optical_fibre_total_internal_reflection_bridge_nano | nano | — |  | T19 reflection mechanism extends to T42 TIR + T50 optical-fibre communication (BSNL + ISRO satellite-to-ground). | [reflection_at_boundary_atomic] | — |  |

## T20 — Fluid Mechanics  *(Class 11)*

*10 atomic + 21 nano = 31 concepts.*

| Concept ID | Type | Sim | Diamond | Description (what it teaches) | Requires | Required-by | Targets misconception |
|---|---|:---:|:---:|---|---|---|---|
| **fluid_pressure_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | Pressure in fluid: P = F/A; depth-dependence P = P₀ + ρgh (hydrostatic). Acts equally in all directions at a point. SI: Pa = N/m². Atmospheric pressure ≈ 10⁵ Pa. | [stress_strain_atomic(T18), newton_second_law_atomic(T11)] | [pascals_law_atomic, archimedes_buoyancy_atomic, bernoullis_principle_atomic] |  |
| ↳ depth_pressure_rho_g_h_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Pressure increases linearly with depth: P(h) = P₀ + ρgh. Indian-Navy submarine context: 10 m water = 1 atm; INS Arihant at 300 m ≈ 31 atm. | [fluid_pressure_atomic] | [archimedes_buoyancy_atomic] |  |
| ↳ atmospheric_pressure_torricelli_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Torricelli mercury barometer: 760 mm Hg = 1 atm = 1.013 × 10⁵ Pa. Indian meteorology stations (IMD network) measure surface pressure for weather prediction. | [fluid_pressure_atomic] | — |  |
| **pascals_law_atomic** | atomic | ✅ | 💎 | Pressure applied at any point in enclosed incompressible fluid transmits undiminished to every other point. F_out/A_out = F_in/A_in → mechanical advantage = A_out/A_in. | [fluid_pressure_atomic] | [hydraulic_lift_application_nano] | pressure increases force proportionally to area |
| ↳ hydraulic_lift_application_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Tata Motors + Ashok Leyland workshop hydraulic-lift systems use Pascal's law. Maruti/Hyundai service stations India-wide: 100 kg force on 10 cm² piston → 10,000 kg lift on 1 m² piston. | [pascals_law_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ hydraulic_brakes_jcb_nano | nano | — |  | JCB India earthmovers + Tata trucks + Indian Railways braking systems use hydraulic-pressure transmission. JCB Pune manufactures excavators with Pascal-law hydraulics. | [pascals_law_atomic] | — |  |
| **archimedes_buoyancy_atomic** | atomic | ✅ | 💎 | Object immersed in fluid experiences upward buoyant force equal to weight of fluid displaced: F_b = ρ_fluid × V_displaced × g. Floats if ρ_object < ρ_fluid (effective density via shape). | [fluid_pressure_atomic, depth_pressure_rho_g_h_nano] | [submarine_buoyancy_nano] | heavier objects sink |
| ↳ iron_ship_floats_hull_shape_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Steel hull of cargo ship: total density (steel + air interior) << water density. INS Vikrant aircraft carrier displacement 45,000 tonnes — floats per Archimedes. **Cognitive scaffold nano.** | [archimedes_buoyancy_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ submarine_buoyancy_ballast_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Indian Navy submarines (INS Arihant, Kalvari class) adjust buoyancy by flooding/blowing ballast tanks — controls effective ρ. | [archimedes_buoyancy_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ hot_air_balloon_density_nano | nano | — |  | Hot air at 100°C has ρ ≈ 0.95 kg/m³ vs cold air at 25°C ρ ≈ 1.18 kg/m³ → buoyancy lift. Indian Hot Air Balloon Festival (Pushkar Rajasthan). | [archimedes_buoyancy_atomic] | — |  |
| **continuity_equation_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | Mass conservation in incompressible flow: A₁v₁ = A₂v₂. Volume-flow-rate Q = Av is constant along tube. | [fluid_pressure_atomic] | [bernoullis_principle_atomic] |  |
| ↳ river_narrowing_application_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Ganges narrows at Rishikesh + Haridwar gorges → flow speeds up; widens at delta → slows. Same flow rate. | [continuity_equation_atomic] | — |  |
| **bernoullis_principle_atomic** | atomic | ✅ | 💎 | P + ½ρv² + ρgh = constant along streamline (incompressible + non-viscous + steady flow). Pressure DROPS where velocity rises. | [continuity_equation_atomic, work_energy_theorem(T13), fluid_pressure_atomic] | [aviation_lift_nano, venturi_flowmeter_nano, atomiser_nano] | Bernoulli applies to any flow |
| ↳ aviation_lift_application_nano | nano | ✅ |  | HAL Tejas + Boeing 787 Air India + IndiGo A320 wing: curved upper surface → faster airflow → lower pressure → net upward lift. **Approximation only** (Bernoulli partially explains; angle-of-attack also critical). | [bernoullis_principle_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ venturi_flowmeter_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Pipe narrowing → higher v → lower P → manometer reading gives flow rate. Used in Indian petroleum (IOCL refineries) + water-supply (Hindustan Tin Works) + medical IV drips. | [bernoullis_principle_atomic, continuity_equation_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ atomiser_spray_paint_nano | nano | — |  | Asian Paints + Berger Paints spray-gun atomisers; horizontal high-v airflow creates low pressure that sucks paint up nozzle. Also IPL stadium watering sprinklers. | [bernoullis_principle_atomic] | — |  |
| **viscosity_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | F = ηA(dv/dy); shear stress = η × velocity-gradient. SI: Pa·s. η_water(20°C) ≈ 10⁻³ Pa·s; η_honey ≈ 10 Pa·s; η_air ≈ 1.8 × 10⁻⁵ Pa·s. Temperature-dependent (liquids: η ↓ as T ↑; gases: η ↑ as T ↑). | [shear_stress_nano(T18), fluid_pressure_atomic] | [stokes_terminal_velocity_atomic, reynolds_number_atomic] | viscosity = thickness |
| ↳ engine_oil_grading_application_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Indian Oil (IOCL) + HP + BP engine-oil SAE grades: 10W-30, 5W-40 — multi-grade oils with η-T behaviour spec'd for Indian climate (40-45°C summer). | [viscosity_atomic] | — |  |
| **stokes_terminal_velocity_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | Drag on small sphere in viscous fluid: F_drag = 6πηrv (low-Re limit). Terminal v: v_t = (2/9)·(ρ_sphere − ρ_fluid)gr²/η when drag = net weight. | [viscosity_atomic, newton_second_law_atomic(T11)] | [parachute_application_nano, raindrop_terminal_v_nano] |  |
| ↳ raindrop_terminal_velocity_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Monsoon raindrop (r ≈ 2 mm) reaches v_t ≈ 6-10 m/s in seconds; without air resistance would fall at >100 m/s from 1 km cloud. **Indian monsoon context.** | [stokes_terminal_velocity_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ parachute_drdo_application_nano | nano | — |  | DRDO + Indian Army parachute design (ADRDE Agra) uses Stokes/quadratic-drag scaling for terminal v ≈ 5 m/s landing speed. | [stokes_terminal_velocity_atomic] | — |  |
| **reynolds_number_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | Re = ρvD/η; dimensionless ratio of inertial to viscous forces. Re < 2000: laminar; Re > 4000: turbulent; 2000-4000: transition. Predicts onset of turbulence. | [viscosity_atomic, continuity_equation_atomic] | — | Re predicts flow type uniquely |
| ↳ pipe_flow_water_supply_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Indian municipal water supply (Bangalore BWSSB, Delhi DJB, Mumbai BMC): pipe design uses Re to prevent turbulent losses + pump-power-spec. | [reynolds_number_atomic] | — |  |
| **surface_tension_atomic** | atomic | ✅ | 💎 | T = F/L (force per unit length along surface); equivalently energy per unit area (J/m²). Origin: net inward cohesive force on surface molecules. T_water ≈ 73 × 10⁻³ N/m at 20°C. | [fluid_pressure_atomic] | [capillary_action_atomic, droplet_spherical_nano, water_strider_nano] | surface tension floats things |
| ↳ droplet_spherical_shape_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Surface tension minimises surface area → sphere for fixed volume. Rain droplets, mercury beads, soap bubbles all approach spherical. | [surface_tension_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ water_strider_insect_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Water strider (पानी का कीड़ा — observable in Indian ponds) walks on water: weight = surface-tension support across legs. Demonstrates scale-dependence. | [surface_tension_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ soap_bubble_excess_pressure_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Inside soap bubble: ΔP = 4T/R (two surfaces). Inside water droplet: ΔP = 2T/R (one surface). Smaller bubble → higher inside pressure. | [surface_tension_atomic] | — |  |
| **capillary_action_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | Capillary rise in narrow tube: h = 2T cosθ / (ρgr). Angle of contact θ determines rise (θ<90°: rise) or depression (θ>90°: e.g., mercury in glass). | [surface_tension_atomic, fluid_pressure_atomic] | [soil_water_uptake_nano, plant_xylem_nano] |  |
| ↳ soil_water_uptake_agricultural_nano | nano | ✅ |  | ICAR (Indian Council of Agricultural Research) studies capillary rise in soil — controls irrigation efficiency. Drip irrigation (Jain Irrigation Jalgaon) leverages capillary distribution. | [capillary_action_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ plant_xylem_capillary_nano | nano | — |  | Plant xylem tubes lift water from roots to leaves via capillary + transpiration. Critical for Indian farming + horticulture. | [capillary_action_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ blotting_paper_chromatography_nano | nano | — |  | Paper chromatography (Class 11-12 lab + DRDO forensics) uses capillary rise in paper fibres to separate dye components. | [capillary_action_atomic] | — |  |

| **traveling_wave_equation_y_equals_f_t_minus_x_over_v** | atomic | ✅ |  | The general form of a wave traveling in +x direction at speed v: y(x,t) = f(t − x/v).
