| **longitudinal_wave_speed_in_fluid_v_equals_sqrt_B_over_rho** | atomic | ✅ |  | Speed of longitudinal wave in a fluid: v = √(B/ρ). B = bulk modulus, ρ = density. | longitudinal_wave_definition_particles_parallel, `bulk_modulus` [Topic-18 Elasticity] | newton_laplace_speed_of_sound_correction |  |
| **longitudinal_wave_speed_in_solid_rod_v_equals_sqrt_Y_over_rho** | atomic | ✅ |  | Speed of longitudinal wave in a long solid rod: v = √(Y/ρ). Y = Young's modulus. | longitudinal_wave_definition_particles_parallel, `youngs_modulus` [Topic-18 Elasticity] | newton_laplace_speed_of_sound_correction |  |
| **newton_laplace_speed_of_sound_correction** | atomic | ✅ |  | Newton's formula v = √(P/ρ) ≈ 280 m/s underestimates by ~15%. Laplace correction: process is adiabatic, not isothermal → B_adiabatic = γP → v = √(γP/ρ) = 331 m/s (matches measurement). | longitudinal_wave_speed_in_fluid_v_equals_sqrt_B_over_rho, `adiabatic_process` [Topic-25 Thermodynamics] | — |  |
| **principle_of_superposition_two_waves_pass_through_each_other** | atomic | ✅ |  | When two or more waves traverse the same medium simultaneously, the displacement of any element is the algebraic sum of displacements due to each wave. The waves pass through unmodified after overlap. | traveling_wave_equation_y_equals_f_t_minus_x_over_v, sinusoidal_wave_y_equals_a_sin_kx_minus_omega_t_plus_phi | — |  |
| ↳ displacements_add_algebraically_pointwise | nano | ✅ |  | At each (x,t), y_total = y_1 + y_2 + ... + y_n | principle_of_superposition_two_waves_pass_through_each_other | principle_of_superposition_two_waves_pass_through_each_other |  |
| ↳ linear_waves_only_obey_superposition | nano | ✅ |  | Superposition holds for small-amplitude (linear) waves. Non-linear waves (huge amplitude) don't simply add. | principle_of_superposition_two_waves_pass_through_each_other | principle_of_superposition_two_waves_pass_through_each_other |  |
| ↳ two_pulses_pass_through_each_other_then_continue | nano | ✅ |  | Two opposite-shape pulses momentarily cancel at overlap (y_total = 0 across string), then continue unchanged | principle_of_superposition_two_waves_pass_through_each_other, displacements_add_algebraically_pointwise | principle_of_superposition_two_waves_pass_through_each_other |  |
| **particle_velocity_from_partial_derivative** | atomic | ✅ |  | v_P(x,t) = ∂y/∂t = Aω cos(kx − ωt + φ) | sinusoidal_wave_y_equals_a_sin_kx_minus_omega_t_plus_phi, wave_velocity_vs_particle_velocity_distinction, `partial_derivative` (math-tools) | particle_acceleration_in_sinusoidal_wave_a_p_equals_minus_omega_squared_y |  |
| ↳ partial_derivative_t_treats_x_constant | nano | ✅ |  | ∂/∂t means hold x fixed (look at one particle); d/dt would mean follow a moving point | particle_velocity_from_partial_derivative, `partial_derivative` | particle_velocity_from_partial_derivative |  |
| **particle_acceleration_in_sinusoidal_wave_a_p_equals_minus_omega_squared_y** | atomic | ✅ |  | a_P = ∂²y/∂t² = −ω² · y(x,t). Same form as SHM — each particle executes SHM. | particle_velocity_from_partial_derivative | — |  |
| **two_graphs_y_vs_x_at_fixed_t_AND_y_vs_t_at_fixed_x** | atomic | ✅ |  | Two visualizations of the same wave: (i) y-vs-x at fixed time (snapshot — shows wavelength λ); (ii) y-vs-t at fixed position (single particle's SHM — shows period T). Same equation, different "slice". | sinusoidal_wave_y_equals_a_sin_kx_minus_omega_t_plus_phi, wave_velocity_vs_particle_velocity_distinction | — |  |
| ↳ y_x_graph_slope_is_partial_dy_dx | nano | ✅ |  | On the y-x snapshot, slope = ∂y/∂x at that point (not dy/dx since y is a 2-variable function) | two_graphs_y_vs_x_at_fixed_t_AND_y_vs_t_at_fixed_x, partial_derivative_t_treats_x_constant | two_graphs_y_vs_x_at_fixed_t_AND_y_vs_t_at_fixed_x, v_P_equals_minus_v_wave_times_slope |  |
| ↳ y_t_graph_slope_is_particle_velocity | nano | ✅ |  | On the y-t graph at fixed x, slope = ∂y/∂t = particle velocity | two_graphs_y_vs_x_at_fixed_t_AND_y_vs_t_at_fixed_x, particle_velocity_from_partial_derivative | two_graphs_y_vs_x_at_fixed_t_AND_y_vs_t_at_fixed_x |  |
| ↳ phase_difference_from_path_difference_phi_equals_2pi_over_lambda_times_delta_x | nano | ✅ |  | Two particles at distance Δx on the same y-x graph have phase difference φ = (2π/λ)·Δx | two_graphs_y_vs_x_at_fixed_t_AND_y_vs_t_at_fixed_x, wavelength_lambda_min_distance_same_phase | two_graphs_y_vs_x_at_fixed_t_AND_y_vs_t_at_fixed_x |  |
| ↳ phase_difference_from_time_interval_phi_equals_2pi_over_T_times_delta_t | nano | ✅ |  | Same particle at two times Δt has phase difference φ = (2π/T)·Δt | two_graphs_y_vs_x_at_fixed_t_AND_y_vs_t_at_fixed_x, angular_frequency_omega_period_relation | two_graphs_y_vs_x_at_fixed_t_AND_y_vs_t_at_fixed_x |  |
| **energy_density_in_wave_u_equals_half_rho_omega_squared_A_squared** | atomic | ✅ |  | Energy per unit volume in a sinusoidal wave: u = ½ρω²A². Comes from SHM energy ½kx² applied to each particle. | sinusoidal_wave_y_equals_a_sin_kx_minus_omega_t_plus_phi, `SHM_energy` [Topic-20] | power_transmitted_in_wave_P_equals_half_rho_omega_squared_A_squared_S_v |  |
| **power_transmitted_in_wave_P_equals_half_rho_omega_squared_A_squared_S_v** | atomic | ✅ |  | Average power = ½ρω²A²·S·v (S = cross-sectional area). Alternative form on string: P_av = 2π²μvA²ν². | energy_density_in_wave_u_equals_half_rho_omega_squared_A_squared, transverse_wave_speed_on_string_v_equals_sqrt_T_over_mu | — |  |

## T22 — Superposition Standing Waves  *(Class 11)*

*7 atomic + 12 nano = 19 concepts.*

| Concept ID | Type | Sim | Diamond | Description (what it teaches) | Requires | Required-by | Targets misconception |
|---|---|:---:|:---:|---|---|---|---|
| **superposition_principle_atomic** | atomic | ✅ | 💎 | When two or more waves traverse the same medium, the resultant displacement at any point at any time = vector sum of individual displacements. y(x,t) = y₁(x,t) + y₂(x,t) + ... Follows from linearity of wave equation (T19). | [wave_equation_pde_atomic(T19), travelling_wave_function_atomic(T19)] | [standing_waves_string_atomic, beats_atomic, interference_pattern(T44 cross-link)] |  |
| ↳ two_pulse_crossing_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Two pulses approach + cross: at the moment of overlap, displacements add (constructive if same sign; destructive if opposite). After crossing, each pulse continues unchanged — **waves pass through each other**. | [superposition_principle_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ boundary_reflection_transmission_coefficients_nano | nano | ✅ |  | At light↔heavy string junction: reflection coefficient r = (v₂−v₁)/(v₂+v₁); transmission coefficient t = 2v₂/(v₂+v₁). Energy conservation: r²+t²·(v₁/v₂)·(μ₂/μ₁)·... | [superposition_principle_atomic, reflection_at_boundary_atomic(T19), wave_speed_string_atomic(T19)] | — |  |
| **standing_waves_string_atomic** | atomic | ✅ | 💎 | Two oppositely-travelling waves of equal amplitude/frequency superpose to give: y(x,t) = 2A sin(kx) cos(ωt). **Spatial envelope sin(kx) determines amplitude pattern; time-factor cos(ωt) makes whole pattern oscillate in place. No energy translation.** | [superposition_principle_atomic, reflection_at_boundary_atomic(T19)] | [nodes_antinodes_atomic, normal_modes_atomic, melde_experiment_atomic] | standing wave doesn't transport energy |
| ↳ counter_propagating_pair_construction_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Standing wave construction: y₁(x,t) = A sin(kx − ωt) [right-moving] + y₂(x,t) = A sin(kx + ωt) [left-moving from reflection] → 2A sin(kx) cos(ωt). Trig identity: sin(A−B) + sin(A+B) = 2 sin(A) cos(B). | [standing_waves_string_atomic, travelling_wave_function_atomic(T19)] | — |  |
| ↳ energy_localised_not_translated_nano | nano | ✅ |  | At any node, both kinetic + potential energy of string-particle are zero. At antinode, particle KE oscillates max ↔ 0; PE oscillates 0 ↔ max — total energy of segment constant; localised. No power flow across nodes. | [standing_waves_string_atomic, wave_energy_power_atomic(T19)] | — |  |
| **nodes_antinodes_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | **Nodes:** positions where sin(kx) = 0 → x = 0, λ/2, λ, ... (spacing λ/2). **Antinodes:** sin(kx) = ±1 → x = λ/4, 3λ/4, 5λ/4, ... (also λ/2 spacing). Antinodes between adjacent nodes. | [standing_waves_string_atomic, particle_vs_wave_velocity_atomic(T19)] | — | nodes at boundaries always |
| ↳ fixed_vs_free_boundary_pattern_nano | nano | ✅ |  | **Fixed-fixed string** (sitar): node at both ends; allowed wavelengths λ_n = 2L/n. **Open-open pipe** (flute, hollow tube): antinode at both ends; same λ_n = 2L/n but pressure pattern flipped. **Open-closed pipe** (clarinet, single-end closed): node at closed end, antinode at open end; only odd harmonics λ_n = 4L/(2n−1). | [nodes_antinodes_atomic, standing_waves_string_atomic] | — |  |
| **normal_modes_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | Standing-wave allowed frequencies on fixed-fixed string of length L: f_n = n·v/(2L), n = 1, 2, 3, ... **Harmonics:** f_1 = fundamental; f_2 = 2nd harmonic = 1st overtone; etc. For open-closed pipe: f_n = (2n−1)·v/(4L), only odd harmonics. | [standing_waves_string_atomic, wave_speed_string_atomic(T19), nodes_antinodes_atomic] | [musical_instrument_harmonics_application_nano] |  |
| ↳ harmonics_overtones_terminology_nano | nano | ✅ |  | f_n = n·f_1: n=1 is fundamental (1st harmonic); n=2 is 1st overtone = 2nd harmonic; etc. **Terminology trap:** "nth harmonic" = nth multiple of f_1; "nth overtone" = (n+1)th harmonic. Cognitive scaffold for student. | [normal_modes_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ musical_instrument_harmonics_application_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Sitar/veena/violin: many harmonics simultaneously (tone "timbre"); fundamental gives pitch; relative amplitudes of harmonics determine tonal character (sitar vs violin sound DIFFERENT at same pitch). **ITC Sangeet Research Academy + IIT-Bombay music-cognition** research. | [normal_modes_atomic, musical_string_tuning_application_nano(T19)] | — |  |
| **beats_atomic** | atomic | ✅ | 💎 | Superposition of two waves of nearly-equal frequency f₁, f₂ at the same point: amplitude envelope oscillates at f_envelope = (f₁−f₂)/2, but intensity oscillates at f_beat = \|f₁−f₂\|. Audible as "wah-wah" pulsation. | [superposition_principle_atomic, wave_parameters_atomic(T19)] | [tabla_tuning_application_nano] | beats happen in space |
| ↳ tabla_tuning_application_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Tabla, sitar, violin tuning by ear: master tuner adjusts string until beats with reference frequency slow to zero — at zero beats, frequencies match. **Indian-classical-music universal practice; ITC Sangeet + Doordarshan music broadcasts.** | [beats_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ piano_tuner_beat_detection_nano | nano | — |  | Piano tuners (rare in India but exists) use beats between adjacent strings to set "equal temperament" — slight frequency offsets give consonant intervals. Same physics as tabla tuning. | [beats_atomic] | — |  |
| **melde_experiment_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | Standing waves on a string driven by electrical tuning fork at one end; other end attached to weight via pulley. Standing-wave pattern forms when f_driver matches one of f_n = n·v/(2L). Classic Indian Class-11/12 physics-lab apparatus. | [normal_modes_atomic, standing_waves_string_atomic, wave_speed_string_atomic(T19)] | — |  |
| ↳ resonance_amplitude_buildup_nano | nano | ✅ |  | At f_driver = f_n: forced oscillator (string) responds with very large amplitude (theoretically infinite without damping; practically limited by air drag + internal losses). Bridges to T17 SHM driven-damped-oscillator. | [melde_experiment_atomic, normal_modes_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ acoustic_resonator_cavity_application_nano | nano | — |  | Microwave cavity resonators (used in Indian Space Programme + DRDO radar): same standing-wave physics in 3D box. Cavity length tunes resonant frequency. | [melde_experiment_atomic, normal_modes_atomic] | — |  |
| **wave_interference_quantitative_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | Two-source superposition at point P: y_P = y₁ + y₂. Path difference Δ → phase difference φ = 2πΔ/λ. **Constructive interference:** Δ = nλ → amplitude = 2A (intensity 4× single-source). **Destructive:** Δ = (n+½)λ → amplitude = 0. **Foundation for T44 wave optics YDSE.** | [superposition_principle_atomic, wave_parameters_atomic(T19)] | [interference_pattern_YDSE(T44 — already)] |  |
| ↳ intensity_pattern_cos_squared_nano | nano | ✅ |  | I(φ) = 4I₀ cos²(φ/2) for two coherent equal-amplitude sources. Pattern oscillates between 0 (destructive) and 4I₀ (constructive). **Already validated in T44 wave optics YDSE.** | [wave_interference_quantitative_atomic] | — |  |

## T23 — Sound Waves  *(Class 11)*

*6 atomic + 19 nano = 25 concepts.*

| Concept ID | Type | Sim | Diamond | Description (what it teaches) | Requires | Required-by | Targets misconception |
|---|---|:---:|:---:|---|---|---|---|
| **longitudinal_wave_sound_atomic** | atomic | ✅ | 💎 | Sound is a longitudinal mechanical wave: particles of medium oscillate parallel to direction of energy propagation, creating alternating compressions (high pressure) + rarefactions (low pressure). Requires elastic medium (gas, liquid, solid) — cannot travel through vacuum. | [wave_equation_pde_atomic(T19), travelling_wave_function_atomic(T19)] | [pressure_displacement_dual_atomic, speed_of_sound_newton_laplace_atomic, pipe_acoustic_resonance_atomic, intensity_loudness_db_atomic, doppler_effect_sound_atomic] | longitudinal-vs-transverse |
| ↳ compression_rarefaction_pattern_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Compression = particles momentarily bunched → local pressure increase ΔP > 0. Rarefaction = particles momentarily spread → ΔP < 0. Pattern travels at v_sound; individual particles oscillate in-place ±s₀. **Mass NOT transported; only the disturbance.** | [longitudinal_wave_sound_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ vacuum_no_sound_demonstration_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Bell jar with vacuum pump: ringing bell becomes silent as air is evacuated — proves sound needs medium. Contrast with light (EM wave) which propagates through vacuum. **Indian CBSE Class-11 lab demo.** | [longitudinal_wave_sound_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ ultrasound_infrasound_audible_bands_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Audible band: ~20 Hz–20 kHz (declines with age). **Ultrasound > 20 kHz** (AIIMS medical imaging, industrial NDT, dog whistles, bat echolocation). **Infrasound < 20 Hz** (elephant communication, IMD earthquake-precursor monitoring, volcano monitoring). Same physics; different perception. | [longitudinal_wave_sound_atomic] | — |  |
| **pressure_displacement_dual_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | Sound wave can be described two equivalent ways: **Displacement wave** s(x,t) = s₀ sin(kx−ωt); **Pressure wave** p(x,t) = p₀ cos(kx−ωt) = BAks₀ cos(kx−ωt) (where B = bulk modulus). **Key:** pressure leads displacement by π/2 → pressure-antinode coincides with displacement-node. | [longitudinal_wave_sound_atomic, wave_equation_pde_atomic(T19)] | [pipe_acoustic_resonance_atomic, intensity_loudness_db_atomic] | pressure peaks where displacement peaks |
| ↳ phase_shift_pi_over_2_visualisation_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Stationary snapshot: where particles are maximally displaced (compression edge), they are momentarily at rest — local pressure neither max nor min. Where particles cross equilibrium (max velocity), they bunch densely → max pressure. **Visualisation requires double-track animation (displacement + pressure synchronised).** | [pressure_displacement_dual_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ pressure_amplitude_p0_formula_nano | nano | ✅ |  | p₀ = BAks₀ where B = bulk modulus, k = wavenumber, s₀ = displacement amplitude. For air at STP: B ≈ 1.42×10⁵ Pa; typical conversational speech p₀ ≈ 0.01 Pa with s₀ ≈ 10⁻⁸ m — extraordinarily small displacement, measurable pressure. | [pressure_displacement_dual_atomic, longitudinal_wave_sound_atomic] | — |  |
| **speed_of_sound_newton_laplace_atomic** | atomic | ✅ | 💎 | Speed of sound in gas: **Newton (1687) — isothermal assumption:** v = √(P/ρ) → predicts 280 m/s at STP (wrong; measured 332 m/s, off by ~16%). **Laplace (1816) — adiabatic correction:** v = √(γP/ρ) where γ = Cp/Cv ≈ 1.40 for air → predicts 332 m/s (matches experiment). Physical reason: sound oscillations are too rapid for heat exchange → adiabatic, not isothermal. | [longitudinal_wave_sound_atomic, ideal_gas_law(T27), adiabatic_process(T26)] | [pipe_acoustic_resonance_atomic, doppler_effect_sound_atomic] |  |
| ↳ temperature_dependence_v_sqrt_T_nano | nano | ✅ |  | From v = √(γRT/M): v ∝ √T (at fixed γ, M). **Indian-classroom-grade rule:** v at temperature T (in K) = v₀·√(T/T₀). At T = 0°C: v = 332 m/s; at T = 30°C (Indian summer): v ≈ 350 m/s. Audible to musicians during humid Indian summers. | [speed_of_sound_newton_laplace_atomic, ideal_gas_law(T27)] | — |  |
| ↳ humidity_density_dependence_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Humid air has slightly LOWER mean molar mass (water vapour M=18 < dry-air M=29) → v slightly HIGHER in humid air. ~0.4% increase per 50% RH change. Negligible in classroom, measurable in precision acoustic engineering (CSIR-NPL standards). | [speed_of_sound_newton_laplace_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ speed_in_liquids_solids_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Liquids: v = √(B/ρ); water ≈ 1480 m/s. Solids: v = √(Y/ρ); steel ≈ 5960 m/s. **Solids fastest** because Young's modulus >> bulk modulus of gas. Anchor: DRDO submarine SONAR uses water sound-speed; Indian Railways rail-track sound transmission detectable miles away (rail-ear-press folklore). | [speed_of_sound_newton_laplace_atomic, elasticity_atomic(T18)] | — |  |
| **pipe_acoustic_resonance_atomic** | atomic | ✅ | 💎 | Air columns inside pipes support standing waves of sound: pressure node ↔ displacement antinode (and vice versa) at boundaries. **Open-open pipe (flute, bansuri):** displacement antinodes at both ends → f_n = nv/(2L), all harmonics. **Open-closed pipe (clarinet, bottle):** displacement node at closed end + antinode at open end → f_n = (2n−1)v/(4L), only odd harmonics. **End-correction:** effective length = L + 0.6r at each open end. | [pressure_displacement_dual_atomic, standing_waves_string_atomic(T22), normal_modes_atomic(T22), nodes_antinodes_atomic(T22)] | — |  |
| ↳ bansuri_shehnai_harmonics_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Indian bamboo bansuri (Hariprasad Chaurasia tradition) is open-open pipe — full harmonic series accessible (the flute "sweetness"). Shehnai is open-closed-conical-bore — only odd harmonics dominate giving distinctive "nasal" timbre. **ITC Sangeet Research Academy formal pedagogy.** | [pipe_acoustic_resonance_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ end_correction_explanation_nano | nano | ✅ |  | At the open end, the air column extends slightly beyond the physical mouth (because pressure-equalisation extends into open air). End-correction ≈ 0.6r where r = pipe radius. **Indian Class-11/12 physics lab resonance-column experiment with water column directly measures this.** | [pipe_acoustic_resonance_atomic, nodes_antinodes_atomic(T22)] | — |  |
| ↳ resonance_column_apparatus_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Standard CBSE/ISC + IIT physics-lab apparatus: vertical glass tube + adjustable water reservoir; tuning fork held over open top; resonance heard when air-column length = λ/4, 3λ/4, ... Measures v_sound from known fork frequency. Tests Laplace formula directly. | [pipe_acoustic_resonance_atomic, speed_of_sound_newton_laplace_atomic] | — |  |
| **intensity_loudness_db_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | **Intensity** I = power/area = ½ρωv·s₀² = p₀²/(2ρv) [W/m²]. **Decibel scale (logarithmic):** β = 10 log₁₀(I/I₀) with reference I₀ = 10⁻¹² W/m² (threshold of human hearing). **Loudness perception is approximately logarithmic** (Weber-Fechner law). Conversational speech ≈ 60 dB; rock concert ≈ 110 dB; pain threshold ≈ 120 dB. | [pressure_displacement_dual_atomic, wave_energy_power_atomic(T19), longitudinal_wave_sound_atomic] | [doppler_effect_sound_atomic (intensity-shift extension)] | double intensity = double dB |
| ↳ log_scale_intuition_db_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Each 10 dB = 10× intensity. 60 dB → 70 dB is 10× more intense, perceived as ~2× louder. Common Indian-context: autorickshaw horn at 1 m ≈ 100 dB; Mumbai traffic ambient ≈ 75 dB; library ≈ 30 dB. Cognitive scaffold: log scale matches human sensory perception. | [intensity_loudness_db_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ inverse_square_intensity_falloff_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Point source in 3D: I ∝ 1/r² → β decreases by 6 dB per doubling of distance. Why: same energy spreads over surface 4πr². Important for noise-pollution regulation + concert-hall design. **CPCB India noise standards reference this.** | [intensity_loudness_db_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ noise_pollution_indian_standards_nano | nano | — |  | **CPCB (Central Pollution Control Board) India** mandates: residential zones ≤ 55 dB daytime / 45 dB night; commercial 65/55; industrial 75/70; silence-zone (hospitals, schools) 50/40. Enforcement via state pollution-control boards. | [intensity_loudness_db_atomic] | — |  |
| **doppler_effect_sound_atomic** | atomic | ✅ | 💎 | Apparent frequency f' heard by observer differs from source frequency f when source-observer-medium relative motion exists. **General formula:** f' = f·(v ± v_obs)/(v ∓ v_src) where signs depend on directions and v = sound speed in medium. **Asymmetry:** medium is at rest in lab frame — source-moving vs observer-moving give different formulae (not Galilean-equivalent). | [longitudinal_wave_sound_atomic, speed_of_sound_newton_laplace_atomic, wave_parameters_atomic(T19), relative_motion_velocity_atomic(T7 — kinematics relative-motion)] | [sonic_boom_mach_cone_nano, doppler_radar_application_nano, beats_doppler_nano] | source-vs-observer asymmetry due to medium frame |
| ↳ ambulance_siren_passing_by_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Classic anchor: ambulance approaches → f' > f (pitch rises); passes → f' < f (pitch drops). **Indian context:** police siren, ambulance horn, Indian Railways horn-doppler at level crossings — high-pitched-approaching → low-pitched-receding step-change at observer pass-by. | [doppler_effect_sound_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ source_observer_asymmetry_explanation_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Why two formulae? Sound wave is carried by medium (air at rest). If source moves toward observer, wavelength in front compresses (λ' < λ); v_sound unchanged → f' = v/λ' > f. If observer moves toward stationary source, λ unchanged but observer sweeps through wavefronts faster → f' = (v+v_obs)/λ > f. **Different physical mechanisms.** | [doppler_effect_sound_atomic, longitudinal_wave_sound_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ sonic_boom_mach_cone_nano | nano | ✅ |  | When v_src > v_sound (supersonic): wavefronts pile up into a Mach cone of half-angle sin θ = v/v_src. Sonic boom = shockwave reaching observer. **Indian anchor: HAL Tejas LCA + IAF Sukhoi/Rafale supersonic test flights over Pokhran + Bay of Bengal corridor.** | [doppler_effect_sound_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ doppler_radar_application_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Police speed-guns + Indian traffic-radar (Delhi/Mumbai/Bengaluru): emit microwave, measure reflected-wave Doppler shift → vehicle speed. ISRO weather-radar (Doppler weather imaging): wind-velocity from rain-droplet reflection shift. **Same Doppler principle — observer + reflector + source roles inverted.** | [doppler_effect_sound_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ beats_doppler_application_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Apply T22 beats to Doppler: two slightly-detuned tuning forks (e.g., 256 Hz vs 258 Hz) produce 2 Hz beats. If one fork moves, Doppler shifts its f, changing beat rate — classic Indian-physics-lab tuning-fork experiment. **Cross-reference T22 beats_atomic.** | [doppler_effect_sound_atomic, beats_atomic(T22)] | — |  |

## T25 — Thermal Properties  *(Class 11)*

*10 atomic + 19 nano = 29 concepts.*

| Concept ID | Type | Sim | Diamond | Description (what it teaches) | Requires | Required-by | Targets misconception |
|---|---|:---:|:---:|---|---|---|---|
| **temperature_scales_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | Temperature: measure of thermal energy; thermometric property. Three scales: Celsius (water-ice 0°C, boiling 100°C), Kelvin (absolute, 0 K = −273.15°C), Fahrenheit (legacy). T(K) = T(°C) + 273.15. ΔT(K) = ΔT(°C). | [kinetic_temperature_atomic(T27)] | [thermal_expansion_atomic, calorimetry_principle_atomic, all-other-T25-atomics] |  |
| ↳ kelvin_vs_celsius_for_delta_T_nano | nano | ✅ |  | ΔT in Kelvin = ΔT in Celsius (since both scales have 1-unit = 1-K size). All thermal-physics equations use ΔT directly — Kelvin-vs-Celsius doesn't matter for differences. Critical for student. | [temperature_scales_atomic] | [all other T25] |  |
| ↳ clinical_thermometer_application_nano | nano | ✅ |  | AIIMS + apollo + Class-12 lab clinical thermometer: 35-42°C range, mercury or digital. Indian-context: fever monitoring during dengue/COVID waves. | [temperature_scales_atomic] | — |  |
| **thermal_expansion_atomic** | atomic | ✅ | 💎 | Solid bodies expand on heating: ΔL = αL₀ΔT (linear); ΔA = βA₀ΔT (area, β ≈ 2α); ΔV = γV₀ΔT (volume, γ ≈ 3α). Coefficient α depends on material. Steel α ≈ 12 × 10⁻⁶ /K; copper ≈ 17 × 10⁻⁶; aluminum ≈ 23 × 10⁻⁶. | [temperature_scales_atomic] | [rail_track_expansion_nano, anomalous_water_expansion_nano] | α/β/γ independent |
| ↳ linear_area_volumetric_relation_nano | nano | ✅ |  | β = 2α; γ = 3α (to leading order). Derivation: differentiate (L+ΔL)² = L² + 2LΔL + (ΔL)² and (L+ΔL)³ similarly. Cognitive scaffold. | [thermal_expansion_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ rail_track_expansion_application_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Indian Railways 1 km steel rail expands ~1.2 cm per 10°C ΔT. Expansion gaps (4-6 mm) every 13 m rail section. Welded long-rail uses pre-stressing. **Tata Steel + SAIL spec'd to standard α.** | [thermal_expansion_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ anomalous_water_expansion_4c_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Water has MAXIMUM density at 4°C; expands on cooling 4→0°C. Causes ice to float + Indian lake-fish to survive winter beneath ice cap. Critical to monsoon climate. | [thermal_expansion_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ thermal_expansion_liquid_gas_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Liquid γ_water ≈ 207 × 10⁻⁶ /K. Gas: PV = nRT means γ_gas dominated by P-T behaviour (V proportional to T at constant P). **Cross-cluster link to T20 fluid density-T dependence.** | [thermal_expansion_atomic, ideal_gas_equation(T27)] | [heat_convection_atomic] |  |
| **calorimetry_principle_atomic** | atomic | ✅ | 💎 | Heat-lost = Heat-gained in mixing without phase-change: m₁C₁(T₁−T_f) = m₂C₂(T_f−T₂). Conservation of energy applied to thermal interactions. | [temperature_scales_atomic, specific_heat_solid_liquid_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ water_equivalent_application_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Water equivalent W of calorimeter: heat absorbed by calorimeter = W·C_water·ΔT. Standard Indian physics-lab equipment + IIT-Bombay+IIT-Madras Class-11/12 lab kits. | [calorimetry_principle_atomic] | — |  |
| **specific_heat_solid_liquid_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | Q = mCΔT; energy to raise unit mass by unit temperature. Water C ≈ 4186 J/kg·K (exceptionally high); ice ≈ 2100; steam ≈ 2010; iron ≈ 460; copper ≈ 385. **Bridges T26 Cv/Cp gas-specific-heats to operational form.** | [internal_energy_atomic(T26)] | [latent_heat_atomic, calorimetry_principle_atomic] |  |
| ↳ water_high_c_climate_application_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Water's high C anchors Indian monsoon thermal regulation: oceans heat slowly + cool slowly → moderate coastal climates. Cooking: 1 L water at 25°C → 100°C needs 314 kJ. | [specific_heat_solid_liquid_atomic] | — |  |
| **latent_heat_atomic** | atomic | ✅ | 💎 | Q = mL; energy absorbed/released at phase transition WITHOUT temperature change. L_f (fusion) ice→water = 334 kJ/kg. L_v (vaporisation) water→steam = 2260 kJ/kg. | [specific_heat_solid_liquid_atomic] | [pressure_cooker_application_nano] | ice at 0°C = water at 0°C energetically |
| ↳ pressure_cooker_application_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Standard Indian pressure cooker (Hawkins, Prestige): raises boiling-point to ~120°C at 1.5-2 atm; uses L_v released on condensation to cook food faster + with less fuel. | [latent_heat_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ sweat_cooling_evaporation_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Human sweating in Indian-summer (40-45°C): L_v ≈ 2400 kJ/kg at 35°C → evaporative cooling. 1 g sweat removes 2.4 kJ from skin. **Healthcare/physiology Indian context.** | [latent_heat_atomic] | — |  |
| **heat_conduction_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | Fourier's law: Q/t = kA(ΔT/L). k = thermal conductivity. Cu k ≈ 400 W/m·K; Fe ≈ 80; glass ≈ 1; air ≈ 0.025; wool ≈ 0.04 (insulator). | [temperature_scales_atomic, thermal_expansion_atomic] | [building_insulation_nano] |  |
| ↳ thermal_conductor_vs_insulator_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Indian housing materials: brick (k ≈ 0.8) vs concrete (k ≈ 1.4) vs wood (k ≈ 0.13). BIS National Building Code thermal-insulation requirements. | [heat_conduction_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ winter_clothing_woollen_insulation_nano | nano | — |  | Wool sweater + double-layer clothing in North-Indian winter: trapped air (k ≈ 0.025) is the actual insulator, wool just traps. Same principle in thermos flask. | [heat_conduction_atomic] | — |  |
| **heat_convection_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | Bulk-fluid motion driven by buoyancy + thermal gradient transfers heat. Hot fluid rises (lower ρ); cold fluid sinks; circulation moves heat. **Convection IS buoyancy-driven flow.** | [archimedes_buoyancy_atomic(T20), viscosity_atomic(T20), temperature_scales_atomic] | [sea_breeze_monsoon_nano] |  |
| ↳ sea_breeze_land_breeze_monsoon_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Land heats faster than ocean (lower C) → hot air rises over land → cool air flows in from sea = day-time sea breeze. Reverse at night = land breeze. **Indian monsoon is large-scale extension of this.** | [heat_convection_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ room_heater_radiator_application_nano | nano | — |  | Bajaj + Usha room-heaters: hot-air convection circulates room air. North-Indian winter context. | [heat_convection_atomic] | — |  |
| **stefan_boltzmann_atomic** | atomic | ✅ | 💎 | Total power radiated by black/grey body: P = σεAT⁴. σ = 5.67 × 10⁻⁸ W/m²·K⁴. ε = emissivity (1 for blackbody, <1 for grey body). **Bridges to T38 EM Waves** (radiation IS EM). | [temperature_scales_atomic, em_wave_basics(T38)] | [ntpc_boiler_application_nano, wien_displacement_atomic] |  |
| ↳ ntpc_boiler_thermal_application_nano | nano | ✅ |  | NTPC Korba + Tata Power Mundra + BHEL boilers operate at 600°C surface temps; radiative loss σ(T⁴ − T_amb⁴) is major heat-loss source; insulation + reflective coatings critical. | [stefan_boltzmann_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ sun_solar_radiation_isro_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Sun ≈ blackbody at 5778 K → P/A ≈ σT⁴ ≈ 6 × 10⁷ W/m². Solar constant at Earth ≈ 1361 W/m². ISRO satellites + Indian solar-PV plants use this. | [stefan_boltzmann_atomic, em_wave_basics(T38)] | — |  |
| **wien_displacement_atomic** | atomic | ✅ | 💎 | λ_max · T = b (b = 2.898 × 10⁻³ m·K). Peak wavelength of blackbody spectrum shifts inversely with T. Sun (5778 K): λ_max ≈ 500 nm (yellow-green). Earth (300 K): λ_max ≈ 10 μm (infrared). | [stefan_boltzmann_atomic, em_wave_basics(T38)] | [thermal_imaging_application_nano] |  |
| ↳ thermal_imaging_drdo_application_nano | nano | ✅ |  | DRDO + Indian armed forces thermal-imaging night-vision goggles: detect 300-310 K body heat → IR at λ ≈ 9.7 μm. AIIMS COVID screening thermometers use same principle. | [wien_displacement_atomic, stefan_boltzmann_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ imd_satellite_radiometer_nano | nano | ✅ |  | IMD INSAT satellites carry IR radiometers measuring cloud-top temperatures via Wien's-law peak shift → weather prediction. | [wien_displacement_atomic] | — |  |
| **newtons_law_of_cooling_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | dT/dt = −k(T − T_env); small-ΔT-from-environment limit of Stefan-Boltzmann. T(t) = T_env + (T₀ − T_env)·e^(−kt). | [stefan_boltzmann_atomic, calculus_exponential_decay(math-tools)] | — |  |
| ↳ tea_cooling_application_nano | nano | — |  | Hot tea (60°C → 25°C ambient) cools per Newton's law; characteristic time τ ≈ 1/k ≈ 10-15 min for standard Indian tea-cup. | [newtons_law_of_cooling_atomic] | — |  |

## T26 — Thermodynamics  *(Class 11)*

*15 atomic + 18 nano = 33 concepts.*

| Concept ID | Type | Sim | Diamond | Description (what it teaches) | Requires | Required-by | Targets misconception |
|---|---|:---:|:---:|---|---|---|---|
| **zeroth_law_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | Two systems in thermal equilibrium with a third are in equilibrium with each other; temperature is the operational state-variable defining "thermally equilibrated" | — | [internal_energy_atomic, first_law_atomic] |  |
| ↳ temperature_scales_nano | nano | ✅ |  | T(K) = T(°C) + 273.15; T(°F) = (9/5)T(°C) + 32; absolute zero = 0 K = −273.15 °C; Kelvin = SI primary | [zeroth_law_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ primary_thermometer_nano | nano | — |  | CSIR-NPL Delhi maintains India's primary temperature standard (ITS-90 platinum-resistance thermometer); gas thermometer = primary definition basis | [zeroth_law_atomic, temperature_scales_nano] | — |  |
| **internal_energy_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | U = sum of kinetic + potential energies of all molecules; STATE function (path-independent); depends only on (T, V, n) for an ideal gas → depends only on T | [zeroth_law_atomic] | [first_law_atomic, isothermal_process_atomic, adiabatic_process_atomic, entropy_atomic] |  |
| ↳ state_vs_path_function_nano | nano | ✅ |  | State function: U, T, P, V, S (depend only on the state, ΔU = U_f − U_i). Path function: Q, W (depend on the path between states). **Cognitive-error-prevention nano**. | [internal_energy_atomic] | [first_law_atomic, carnot_cycle_atomic] |  |
| **first_law_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | ΔU = Q − W; energy conservation generalised to heat; Q heat ADDED to system, W work DONE BY system | [internal_energy_atomic, work_energy_theorem(T13), state_vs_path_function_nano] | [isothermal_process_atomic, adiabatic_process_atomic, isobaric_process_atomic, isochoric_process_atomic, carnot_cycle_atomic, heat_engine_atomic] |  |
| ↳ first_law_sign_convention_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Physics convention (NCERT/HCV/DCP): Q in = +, W by system = +; ΔU = Q − W. Chemistry convention: Q in = +, W on system = +; ΔU = Q + W. Same physics, opposite sign for W. **Cognitive-error-prevention nano — explicit contrast required.** | [first_law_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ work_done_in_pv_diagram_nano | nano | ✅ |  | W = ∫P dV (area under P-V curve); positive when V increases (expansion), negative when V decreases (compression) | [first_law_atomic, calculus_integration(math-tools)] | [isothermal_process_atomic, adiabatic_process_atomic] |  |
| **isothermal_process_atomic** | atomic | ✅ | 💎 | T = constant; for ideal gas ΔU = 0 → Q = W; W = nRT ln(V_f/V_i); PV = constant (Boyle's law) | [first_law_atomic, ideal_gas_equation(T27), work_done_in_pv_diagram_nano] | [carnot_cycle_atomic, isothermal_vs_adiabatic_contrast_nano] |  |
| ↳ isothermal_indian_radiator_nano | nano | — |  | Slow cooling of a car/scooter radiator at idle ≈ isothermal heat rejection at constant T_engine; Maruti Suzuki / Tata Motors / Bajaj engines designed around isothermal idle | [isothermal_process_atomic] | — |  |
| **adiabatic_process_atomic** | atomic | ✅ | 💎 | Q = 0 (no heat exchange); ΔU = −W; PV^γ = constant; T₁V₁^(γ−1) = T₂V₂^(γ−1); steeper PV-curve than isothermal | [first_law_atomic, specific_heat_atomic, work_done_in_pv_diagram_nano] | [carnot_cycle_atomic, isothermal_vs_adiabatic_contrast_nano, isothermal_atomic, diesel_engine_compression_nano] |  |
| ↳ isothermal_vs_adiabatic_contrast_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Side-by-side PV-overlay: both start at same (P,V), isothermal stays on PV=const, adiabatic on PV^γ=const (steeper, since γ>1). T drops in adiabatic expansion (Q=0 → all work comes from U → U drops → T drops). **Cognitive-error-prevention nano**. | [isothermal_process_atomic, adiabatic_process_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ diesel_engine_compression_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Diesel engine compression-stroke is approximately adiabatic; T rises ~5× to auto-ignition temperature ~500 °C — fuel ignites without spark. Indian Railways WDM/WDG diesel locomotives + Tata/Mahindra/Ashok-Leyland diesel trucks operate on this. | [adiabatic_process_atomic] | — |  |
| **isobaric_process_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | P = constant; W = P·ΔV; ΔU = nCv·ΔT; Q = nCp·ΔT | [first_law_atomic, specific_heat_atomic] | [heat_engine_atomic, indian_pressure_cooker_nano] |  |
| ↳ indian_pressure_cooker_nano | nano | — |  | Pressure-cooker pre-vent: isobaric heating at ~2 atm; raises water boiling point to ~120 °C → faster cooking. Hawkins/Prestige household appliance everywhere in India | [isobaric_process_atomic] | — |  |
| **isochoric_process_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | V = constant; W = 0; ΔU = Q = nCv·ΔT; pressure scales linearly with T | [first_law_atomic, specific_heat_atomic] | [heat_engine_atomic, otto_cycle_combustion_nano] |  |
| ↳ otto_cycle_combustion_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Petrol engine combustion-stroke is approximately isochoric (volume constant during the brief ignition); used in Maruti/Honda/Bajaj petrol engines + Indian 2-wheeler market (~20M units/yr) | [isochoric_process_atomic] | [heat_engine_atomic] |  |
| **specific_heat_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | C = Q/(nΔT); Cv (constant volume) and Cp (constant pressure); Cp − Cv = R (Mayer's relation, ideal gas); γ = Cp/Cv (adiabatic index) | [first_law_atomic, ideal_gas_equation(T27)] | [adiabatic_process_atomic, isobaric_process_atomic, isochoric_process_atomic] |  |
| ↳ mayers_relation_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Cp − Cv = R (per mole, ideal gas); derived from first law applied to isobaric vs isochoric heating | [specific_heat_atomic, isobaric_process_atomic, isochoric_process_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ gamma_for_mono_di_polyatomic_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Monatomic γ = 5/3 (He, Ne, Ar); diatomic γ = 7/5 (N₂, O₂, H₂); polyatomic γ ≈ 4/3 (CO₂, NH₃, CH₄). Bridges to T27 equipartition theorem (f degrees of freedom → Cv = fR/2) | [specific_heat_atomic, equipartition_theorem(T27)] | [adiabatic_process_atomic] |  |
| **carnot_cycle_atomic** | atomic | ✅ | 💎 | 4-stroke reversible cycle: isothermal-expansion (T_hot) → adiabatic-expansion → isothermal-compression (T_cold) → adiabatic-compression. η_Carnot = 1 − T_cold/T_hot | [isothermal_process_atomic, adiabatic_process_atomic, first_law_atomic, state_vs_path_function_nano] | [heat_engine_atomic, second_law_kelvin_planck_atomic, carnot_inequality_nano] |  |
| ↳ carnot_inequality_nano | nano | ✅ |  | η_real ≤ η_Carnot for any heat engine operating between T_hot and T_cold; equality only for reversible engine. Foundation of second-law optimality. | [carnot_cycle_atomic, second_law_kelvin_planck_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ ntpc_thermal_efficiency_nano | nano | ✅ |  | NTPC supercritical coal plants (Sipat, Vindhyachal, Mundra) operate T_hot ~600 °C steam, T_cold ~40 °C cooling water → η_Carnot ~64%, real η ~42-45%. India's ~75% electricity from such cycles. | [carnot_cycle_atomic, carnot_inequality_nano] | — |  |
| **heat_engine_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | Cyclic device that converts Q_hot → W + Q_cold; efficiency η = W/Q_hot = 1 − Q_cold/Q_hot. Refrigerator + heat pump = reverse of heat engine (W input pumps heat cold→hot) | [carnot_cycle_atomic, first_law_atomic, isobaric_process_atomic, isochoric_process_atomic] | [second_law_kelvin_planck_atomic, second_law_clausius_atomic, otto_cycle_combustion_nano, refrigerator_cop_nano] |  |
| ↳ refrigerator_cop_nano | nano | ✅ |  | COP_refrigerator = Q_cold/W; COP_heat_pump = Q_hot/W; COP_HP = COP_R + 1. Voltas/Godrej/LG India refrigerators rated 1-5 BEE stars based on this | [heat_engine_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ bharat_stage_emission_norms_nano | nano | — |  | BS-VI norms (since 2020) constrain heat-engine efficiency curves on Indian Diesel/petrol vehicles — η improvements + emission caps. Indian Railways shifting from WDM diesel to electric (75% route-km AC-electrified) reduces aggregate Carnot losses. | [heat_engine_atomic, carnot_cycle_atomic] | — |  |
| **second_law_kelvin_planck_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | No process exists whose ONLY result is the complete conversion of heat from a single reservoir into work; equivalently, no heat engine has η = 100% | [carnot_cycle_atomic, heat_engine_atomic] | [second_law_clausius_atomic, kp_clausius_equivalence_atomic, entropy_atomic] |  |
| **second_law_clausius_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | No process exists whose ONLY result is the transfer of heat from a colder body to a hotter body; equivalently, no refrigerator works without external W input | [heat_engine_atomic] | [kp_clausius_equivalence_atomic, entropy_atomic] |  |
| **kp_clausius_equivalence_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | Proof that Kelvin-Planck violation ⟺ Clausius violation — assume one, construct a composite engine that violates the other. Establishes the two statements are operationally identical. | [second_law_kelvin_planck_atomic, second_law_clausius_atomic] | — |  |
| **reversible_vs_irreversible_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | Reversible: infinitely slow, no dissipation, system always in equilibrium; can be reversed by infinitesimal change. Irreversible: real processes (friction, heat conduction across finite ΔT, free expansion, mixing) — direction of time emerges | [first_law_atomic, second_law_kelvin_planck_atomic] | [entropy_atomic, carnot_cycle_atomic] |  |
| **entropy_atomic** | atomic | ✅ | 💎 | S = ∫dQ_rev/T (operational definition); ΔS_universe ≥ 0 for any real process; entropy is a STATE function (despite Q being path function — Q_rev/T is path-independent for reversible paths) | [carnot_cycle_atomic, reversible_vs_irreversible_atomic, second_law_kelvin_planck_atomic, state_vs_path_function_nano] | — |  |
| ↳ entropy_of_universe_increases_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Σ ΔS_system + ΔS_surroundings ≥ 0 for any real process; equality only for reversible. Statistical interpretation: entropy = k ln(W) (Boltzmann; T27 territory but cross-link here). | [entropy_atomic, kinetic_theory_statistical_link(T27)] | — |  |
| ↳ entropy_ncert_2023_note_nano | nano | — |  | NCERT 2023 condensed entropy treatment (removed standalone §12.13); HCV2 Ch.26 + DCWT Ch.21 retain full treatment; state boards (Maharashtra HSC, Tamil Nadu, Karnataka PUC, UP, WB) retain — author at full depth for state-board + JEE-Adv | [entropy_atomic] | — |  |

## T27 — Kinetic Theory  *(Class 11)*

*8 atomic + 16 nano = 24 concepts.*

| Concept ID | Type | Sim | Diamond | Description (what it teaches) | Requires | Required-by | Targets misconception |
|---|---|:---:|:---:|---|---|---|---|
| **kt_assumptions_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | Molecules are point particles + identical mass + random motion + elastic collisions + negligible inter-molecular volume vs container volume + Newtonian mechanics applies | — | [kinetic_theory_pressure_atomic, ideal_gas_equation_atomic, mean_free_path_atomic] |  |
| ↳ point_particle_vs_real_molecule_nano | nano | — |  | Real molecules have finite size + intermolecular forces (van der Waals); ideal-gas treatment is the high-T low-P limit | [kt_assumptions_atomic] | — |  |
| **ideal_gas_equation_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | PV = nRT (macroscopic); equivalent forms PV = NkT (per-molecule) and P = ρRT/M (density form). Bundles Boyle, Charles, Avogadro. | [kt_assumptions_atomic] | [kinetic_theory_pressure_atomic, isothermal_process_atomic(T26), isobaric_process_atomic(T26), isochoric_process_atomic(T26)] |  |
| ↳ boyle_charles_avogadro_unification_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Boyle: PV=const at fixed T; Charles: V/T=const at fixed P; Avogadro: V ∝ n at fixed P,T. All three reconciled in PV=nRT. | [ideal_gas_equation_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ universal_gas_constant_R_nano | nano | — |  | R = 8.314 J/(mol·K); k = R/N_A = 1.38 × 10⁻²³ J/K (Boltzmann constant); SI-unit reconciliation | [ideal_gas_equation_atomic] | — |  |
| **kinetic_theory_pressure_atomic** | atomic | ✅ | 💎 | PV = (1/3)Nm⟨v²⟩; pressure as time-averaged momentum-flux from molecular collisions on container walls; central derivation of chapter | [kt_assumptions_atomic, ideal_gas_equation_atomic, momentum_change_in_elastic_collision(T14)] | [kinetic_temperature_atomic, molecular_speed_distribution_atomic] |  |
| ↳ momentum_flux_per_collision_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Single molecule with v_x hits wall: Δp = 2mv_x; collision rate per molecule = v_x/(2L); pressure contribution per molecule = mv_x²/V | [kinetic_theory_pressure_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ isotropy_factor_one_third_nano | nano | ✅ |  | ⟨v_x²⟩ = ⟨v_y²⟩ = ⟨v_z²⟩ = ⟨v²⟩/3 by isotropy → factor 1/3 in PV = (1/3)Nm⟨v²⟩ | [kinetic_theory_pressure_atomic] | — |  |
| **kinetic_temperature_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | (1/2)m⟨v²⟩ = (3/2)kT — temperature is proportional to per-molecule average translational kinetic energy | [kinetic_theory_pressure_atomic, ideal_gas_equation_atomic] | [molecular_speed_distribution_atomic, equipartition_theorem_atomic, internal_energy_atomic(T26)] |  |
| ↳ temperature_is_translational_ke_not_total_ke_nano | nano | ✅ |  | T relates only to translational KE per (3/2)kT per molecule; rotational + vibrational KE contribute to Cv but not directly to T. **Cognitive-error-prevention nano** — subtle but central misconception. | [kinetic_temperature_atomic, equipartition_theorem_atomic] | — |  |
| **molecular_speed_distribution_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | v_rms = √(3kT/m), v_avg = √(8kT/πm), v_mp = √(2kT/m); inequality v_mp < v_avg < v_rms | [kinetic_temperature_atomic, maxwell_boltzmann_distribution_atomic] | [mean_free_path_atomic, equipartition_theorem_atomic] |  |
| ↳ three_speed_comparison_table_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Side-by-side table: name, formula, numerical-ratio at fixed T (v_mp : v_avg : v_rms ≈ 1.000 : 1.128 : 1.225) | [molecular_speed_distribution_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ rms_speed_n2_o2_at_300k_nano | nano | ✅ |  | N₂ at 300 K: v_rms ≈ 517 m/s; O₂ at 300 K: v_rms ≈ 484 m/s; H₂ at 300 K: v_rms ≈ 1928 m/s (~Earth-escape relevant) | [molecular_speed_distribution_atomic] | — |  |
| **maxwell_boltzmann_distribution_atomic** | atomic | ✅ | 💎 | f(v) = 4π(m/2πkT)^(3/2) v² exp(−mv²/2kT); probability-density of molecular speeds; peaks at v_mp; broadens with T | [kinetic_temperature_atomic, gaussian_distribution(math-tools NEW), integration_of_gaussian(math-tools)] | [molecular_speed_distribution_atomic, equipartition_theorem_atomic] |  |
| ↳ distribution_widens_with_temperature_nano | nano | ✅ |  | At higher T: peak shifts right (higher v_mp), peak height decreases, total area stays = 1; the high-speed tail lengthens | [maxwell_boltzmann_distribution_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ high_speed_tail_for_reaction_rates_nano | nano | — |  | Reaction rates depend on fraction of molecules with KE > activation energy → exponential tail dominates; basis for Arrhenius equation (chemistry) | [maxwell_boltzmann_distribution_atomic] | — |  |
| **equipartition_theorem_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | Each quadratic degree of freedom (KE or PE) contributes (1/2)kT to average per-molecule energy; total U = (f/2)NkT for f dof per molecule | [kinetic_temperature_atomic, molecular_speed_distribution_atomic] | [specific_heat_atomic(T26), gamma_for_mono_di_polyatomic_nano(T26)] |  |
| ↳ degrees_of_freedom_table_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Side-by-side table: Monatomic (3 trans, f=3, γ=5/3, Cv=3R/2). Diatomic rigid (3 trans + 2 rot, f=5, γ=7/5, Cv=5R/2). Diatomic with vib at high T (f=7, γ=9/7, Cv=7R/2). Polyatomic linear (f=5-7), nonlinear (f=6+). **Cognitive-error-prevention nano** — students conflate the three. | [equipartition_theorem_atomic] | [gamma_for_mono_di_polyatomic_nano(T26)] |  |
| ↳ vibrational_modes_kick_in_at_high_t_nano | nano | — |  | Diatomic at room T: f=5 (3 trans + 2 rot). Above ~1000 K: vibrational modes activated → f=7. Explains why Cv is not strictly constant. | [equipartition_theorem_atomic, degrees_of_freedom_table_nano] | — |  |
| **mean_free_path_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | λ = 1/(√2·n·π·d²); average distance a molecule travels between collisions; bridges molecular-scale to bulk-transport phenomena (viscosity, diffusion, conduction) | [kt_assumptions_atomic, ideal_gas_equation_atomic, molecular_speed_distribution_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ mfp_air_at_stp_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Air at STP: λ ≈ 70 nm; n ≈ 2.7 × 10²⁵ /m³; d ≈ 0.37 nm. Validates point-particle assumption (λ ≫ d) | [mean_free_path_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ atmospheric_diffusion_imd_ncmrwf_nano | nano | — |  | MFP increases at high altitude (low n) → diffusion becomes dominant transport mechanism; IMD/NCMRWF weather models use kinetic-theory-derived diffusion coefficients for pollutant transport (CPCB Mumbai/Delhi PM2.5 dispersion) | [mean_free_path_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ vacuum_quality_via_mfp_nano | nano | — |  | Lab vacuum: P=10⁻⁶ torr → λ ~ 50 m ≫ chamber size → molecular-flow regime (vs viscous flow). ISRO satellite-thermal labs + BARC noble-gas separation operate in this regime. | [mean_free_path_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ statistical_entropy_boltzmann_nano | nano | ✅ |  | S = k ln W where W = number of microstates compatible with macrostate. Boltzmann's gravestone equation. Bridges to T26 entropy_atomic. | [maxwell_boltzmann_distribution_atomic, entropy_atomic(T26)] | — |  |

| **infinite_capacitor_via_earthing** | atomic | — |  | DCEM §25.3 inset: one plate earthed → effective capacitance = ∞ since Earth absorbs any charge. Boundary-condition concept atomic. | [two_conductor_capacitor] | — |  |
| **capacitor_confines_field_locally** | atomic | — |  | NCERT §2.16 Point-to-Ponder 2: "Capacitor confines field lines within small region. Thus, even though field may have considerable strength, the PD between conductors is small." Concept of localised field-strength vs global-potential. | [parallel_plate_capacitor] | — |  |
| **dielectric_constant_drops_with_temperature** | atomic | — |  | NCERT §2.16 Point-to-Ponder 6: "dielectric constant decreases if temperature is increased" — explained via polarisation reduction. Thermal disordering atomic. | [dielectric_polarisation, dielectric_increases_capacitance] | — |  |

*28 atomic + 13 nano = 41 concepts.*

| Concept ID | Type | Sim | Diamond | Description (what it teaches) | Requires | Required-by | Targets misconception |

| **force_between_parallel_currents_attract_or_repel** | atomic | ✅ |  | Two parallel wires carrying currents I_a, I_b separated by distance d: force per unit length f = μ₀ I_a I_b / (2πd). **Parallel currents attract; antiparallel currents repel.** | magnetic_force_on_current_carrying_wire_F_equals_IL_cross_B, magnetic_field_long_straight_wire_B_equals_mu0_I_over_2pi_r | ampere_si_unit_definition_from_parallel_currents |  |
| ↳ parallel_currents_attract_antiparallel_repel | nano | ✅ |  | I_a, I_b same direction → attract; opposite direction → repel | force_between_parallel_currents_attract_or_repel, magnetic_force_direction_right_hand_rule | force_between_parallel_currents_attract_or_repel |  |
| ↳ force_per_length_f_equals_mu0_Ia_Ib_over_2pi_d | nano | ✅ |  | f_ba = (μ₀ I_a I_b)/(2πd) per metre length | force_between_parallel_currents_attract_or_repel | force_between_parallel_currents_attract_or_repel, ampere_si_unit_definition_from_parallel_currents |  |
| ↳ force_consistent_with_newton_third_law | nano | ✅ |  | F_ba = −F_ab for steady currents (parallel conductors). Time-varying currents may violate. | force_between_parallel_currents_attract_or_repel | force_between_parallel_currents_attract_or_repel |  |
| **ampere_si_unit_definition_from_parallel_currents** | atomic | partial |  | One ampere = current in each of two parallel wires (1 m apart, vacuum) producing force 2×10⁻⁷ N/m between them. Theoretical definition adopted 1946. | force_between_parallel_currents_attract_or_repel | — |  |
| **magnetic_dipole_potential_energy_U_equals_minus_m_dot_B** | atomic | ✅ |  | Potential energy of dipole in B: U = −m·B = −mB cos θ. Minimum at θ=0 (parallel = stable); max at θ=π. | magnetic_dipole_moment_m_equals_NIA, torque_on_current_loop_tau_equals_m_cross_B | — |  |
| **magnetic_dipole_moment_of_revolving_electron_mu_l_equals_minus_e_over_2m_L** | atomic | ✅ |  | Electron orbiting a nucleus (Bohr model) constitutes a current loop → has magnetic moment μ_l = −(e/2m_e)L, where L = orbital angular momentum. Bohr magneton μ_B = eħ/(2m_e). | magnetic_dipole_moment_m_equals_NIA, `[Topic-47: bohr_model_atom]` | — |  |
| **force_on_curved_wire_in_uniform_B_equals_force_on_straight_wire_between_endpoints** | atomic | ✅ |  | For ANY curved wire ACD in uniform B carrying current i: total force F = i(AD × B), where AD is the straight-line vector from start to end. | magnetic_force_on_current_carrying_wire_F_equals_IL_cross_B, dF_equals_I_dl_cross_B_arbitrary_wire | — |  |
