| ↳ ac_traction_application_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Indian Railways: 25 kV / 50 Hz overhead → on-board step-down + rectifier + traction motor. ~70% of route-km electrified | [transformer_in_ac_atomic, step_up_vs_step_down_nano] | — |  |
| **wattless_current_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | Purely inductive or purely capacitive circuit → cos φ = 0 → P_avg = 0 although I_rms ≠ 0 | [power_in_ac_circuit_atomic, ac_inductor_circuit, ac_capacitor_circuit] | [choke_coil_atomic] |  |
| **choke_coil_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | Inductor used to limit AC current without dissipating power; replaces resistor in fluorescent tube ballast | [ac_inductor_circuit, wattless_current_atomic, ferromagnetism_atomic(T37)] | — |  |
| ↳ choke_in_fluorescent_lamp_nano | nano | — |  | Fluorescent tube ballast = choke coil in series with tube; limits current after ionisation | [choke_coil_atomic] | — |  |

## T41 — Ray Optics Mirrors  *(Class 12)*

*13 atomic + 19 nano = 32 concepts.*

| Concept ID | Type | Sim | Diamond | Description (what it teaches) | Requires | Required-by | Targets misconception |
|---|---|:---:|:---:|---|---|---|---|
| **laws_of_reflection** | atomic | ✅ |  | i=r + normal-incidence + coplanarity. Atomic per RO-G1. EPIC-C STATE_1 wrong belief: "angle of incidence is measured from the mirror surface, not the normal" — universal Class 12 error | — | plane_mirror_image_formation, spherical_mirror_geometry, focal_length_f_equals_R_over_2, [T42:snells_law (analogy)], [T44:huygens_reflection] |  |
| ↳ normal_to_curved_surface | nano | ✅ |  | Normal at any point on a sphere = the radius (line from C through point). Bridge to A4 spherical-mirror geometry | — | laws_of_reflection, focal_length_f_equals_R_over_2 |  |
| ↳ coplanarity_of_incident_normal_reflected | nano | ✅ |  | All three lie in the plane of incidence. Pedagogically subtle — students draw 3D crossings | — | laws_of_reflection |  |
| **plane_mirror_image_formation** | atomic | ✅ |  | v = -u (image distance = object distance on opposite side); lateral inversion; image is virtual, erect, same size. EPIC-C STATE_1 wrong belief: "image is on the mirror surface" — students locate image AT the glass | laws_of_reflection | spherical_mirror_geometry, plane_mirror_velocity_image |  |
| ↳ lateral_inversion_left_right | nano | ✅ |  | Right-hand becomes left-hand. Ambulance "AMBULANCE" mirror-inversion painted text is the Indian-context anchor | — | plane_mirror_image_formation |  |
| ↳ minimum_mirror_height_for_full_image | nano | ✅ |  | h_min = H/2 for full-body view. NCERT Exercise + DCP Q.8 canonical. Indian-context: bathroom mirror sizing | — | plane_mirror_image_formation |  |
| ↳ multiple_images_two_mirrors_at_angle | nano | ✅ |  | N = 360°/θ - 1 (or 360°/θ if asymmetric). Indian-context: kaleidoscope toy + 2-mirror parallel barber-shop infinite reflection | — | plane_mirror_image_formation, laws_of_reflection |  |
| ↳ mirror_rotation_ray_rotates_2theta | nano | ✅ |  | When mirror rotates by θ, reflected ray rotates by 2θ. Classroom galvanometer-scale demonstration; JEE-tested annually | — | plane_mirror_image_formation, laws_of_reflection |  |
| **spherical_mirror_geometry** | atomic | ✅ |  | Pole P, centre of curvature C, radius of curvature R, principal axis, aperture, focal plane. Foundation atomic for all mirror-related math. EPIC-C STATE_1 wrong belief: "the pole is the centre of curvature" — common confusion | laws_of_reflection, normal_to_curved_surface | focal_length_f_equals_R_over_2, cartesian_sign_convention_mirrors, mirror_equation, lateral_magnification_mirror, [T42:refraction_at_spherical_surface] |  |
| ↳ concave_vs_convex_distinction | nano | ✅ |  | Concave: silvered on outside, reflects on inside (caves inward toward C). Convex: silvered on inside, reflects on outside (bulges toward observer). Indian-context: shaving (concave) vs scooter rear-view (convex) | — | spherical_mirror_geometry |  |
| ↳ aperture_must_be_small_for_clean_focus | nano | ✅ |  | Bridge to A11 spherical aberration: if aperture is large, paraxial approximation fails | — | spherical_mirror_geometry, spherical_aberration_mirror |  |
| **focal_length_f_equals_R_over_2** | atomic | ✅ |  | NCERT §9.2.2 derivation via Fig.9.4 geometry. For paraxial rays, f = R/2. The "1/2" surprise — students expect f = R or f = 2R | spherical_mirror_geometry, [math:tan_theta_approx_theta] | cartesian_sign_convention_mirrors, mirror_equation, lateral_magnification_mirror, image_formation_cases_concave_mirror |  |
| ↳ concave_mirror_real_focus | nano | ✅ |  | Parallel rays converge to a real F in front of the mirror. Sign: f negative per Cartesian convention | — | focal_length_f_equals_R_over_2 |  |
| ↳ convex_mirror_virtual_focus | nano | ✅ |  | Parallel rays appear to diverge from a virtual F behind the mirror. Sign: f positive | — | focal_length_f_equals_R_over_2 |  |
| **cartesian_sign_convention_mirrors** | atomic | ✅ |  | Per RO-G2: own atomic. Pole as origin; incident-light direction positive; heights upward positive. The sign table for the 6 image-formation cases. Most common failure point in mirror-formula problems | spherical_mirror_geometry, focal_length_f_equals_R_over_2 | mirror_equation, lateral_magnification_mirror, image_formation_cases_concave_mirror, convex_mirror_image_always_virtual, [T42:sign_convention_lenses (analogous)], [T42:sign_convention_refraction_spherical] |  |
| ↳ direction_of_incident_light_sets_positive_x | nano | ✅ |  | If light travels left-to-right, +x is rightward (and distances toward mirror are positive). If light is reversed (multi-element systems), sign convention can flip mid-problem | — | cartesian_sign_convention_mirrors |  |
| ↳ real_image_in_front_of_mirror_negative_v | nano | ✅ |  | For concave mirror with real object: v negative (image on the same side as object, opposite to incident-light direction beyond pole) | — | cartesian_sign_convention_mirrors, mirror_equation |  |
| **mirror_equation** | atomic | ✅ |  | 1/v + 1/u = 1/f. NCERT derivation via similar triangles A'B'F and ABP. HCV derivation via exterior angle. Per RO-G3: distinct atomic from lens equation despite similar form | spherical_mirror_geometry, focal_length_f_equals_R_over_2, cartesian_sign_convention_mirrors, [math:similar_triangles] | lateral_magnification_mirror, image_formation_cases_concave_mirror, velocity_of_image_in_curved_mirror, [T42:lens_equation (analogous)] |  |
| ↳ derivation_via_similar_triangles | nano | ✅ |  | The MPF ~ A'B'F similarity is the key insight. Pedagogically rigorous | — | mirror_equation |  |
| **lateral_magnification_mirror** | atomic | ✅ |  | m = h'/h = -v/u. Negative m ⇒ inverted (real image); positive m ⇒ erect (virtual image). Per RO-G3 split: lens magnification is m = +v/u (sign convention difference) — common confusion | cartesian_sign_convention_mirrors, mirror_equation | image_formation_cases_concave_mirror, velocity_of_image_in_curved_mirror, [T42:magnification_lens] |  |
| ↳ sign_of_m_tells_image_orientation | nano | ✅ |  | Negative m means inverted; positive m means erect. Magnitude tells size | — | lateral_magnification_mirror |  |
| **image_formation_cases_concave_mirror** | atomic | ✅ |  | Per RO-G4: 6-state atomic. Cases: (i) ∞ → F (real, dim, inv); (ii) beyond C → between F-C (real, dim, inv); (iii) at C → at C (real, same-size, inv); (iv) between C-F → beyond C (real, mag, inv); (v) at F → ∞; (vi) between P-F → virtual, behind mirror, erect, mag. Plus +1 convex case (A9). The CBSE-board canonical case-table | mirror_equation, lateral_magnification_mirror | convex_mirror_image_always_virtual, [T42:lens_image_cases] |  |
| **convex_mirror_image_always_virtual** | atomic | ✅ |  | For any real object: image is virtual, erect, diminished, behind the mirror. Single visual scene. EPIC-C STATE_1 wrong belief: "convex mirror can form a real image with a real object" — fails dimensional check | mirror_equation, lateral_magnification_mirror, image_formation_cases_concave_mirror | plane_mirror_velocity_image, [T43:traffic_safety_optics] |  |
| ↳ scooter_side_mirror_anchor | nano | ✅ |  | Indian-context anchor: every Bajaj/TVS scooter, every auto-rickshaw rear-view. "Objects in mirror are closer than they appear" (the diminished image makes them seem far) | — | convex_mirror_image_always_virtual |  |
| ↳ security_dome_mirror_anchor | nano | ✅ |  | Convex dome mirrors at supermarket corners + Metro station ceilings + bank ATM vestibules. Wide field of view at cost of magnification | — | convex_mirror_image_always_virtual |  |
| **plane_mirror_velocity_image** | atomic | ✅ |  | If object moves with velocity v⃗ relative to mirror, image moves with v⃗ reflected across the mirror plane (parallel component preserved, perpendicular component reversed). Bridge to T6 kinematics. JEE-tested. EPIC-C STATE_1 wrong belief: "image moves at same speed as object" — only true for perpendicular motion | plane_mirror_image_formation, [T6:relative_velocity] | velocity_of_image_in_curved_mirror |  |
| **spherical_aberration_mirror** | atomic | ✅ |  | Per RO-G5: own atomic. Marginal rays focus closer to mirror than paraxial rays; produces caustic curve + circle of least confusion. Fix: parabolic mirror (all parallel rays focus at one point). Indian anchors: automobile headlight reflector (Bajaj/TVS), solar cooker (MNRE SOLBOX program), satellite dish parabola | spherical_mirror_geometry, focal_length_f_equals_R_over_2 | [T42:lens_aberrations], [T43:reflecting_telescope] |  |
| ↳ parabolic_mirror_perfect_for_parallel_rays | nano | ✅ |  | Geometric proof: parabola defined as locus equidistant from focus + directrix ⇒ all parallel rays parallel to axis converge at focus exactly | — | spherical_aberration_mirror |  |
| ↳ reflecting_telescope_uses_parabolic_primary | nano | ✅ |  | Cassegrain telescope: parabolic primary + hyperbolic secondary. Indian anchor: 2.34m reflecting telescope at Kavalur, IIA Bangalore (NCERT §9.9.3 §"Cassegrain") | — | spherical_aberration_mirror, [T43:cassegrain] |  |
| **velocity_of_image_in_curved_mirror** | atomic | ✅ |  | Per RO-G6: own atomic. v_I_longitudinal = m² v_O; v_I_perpendicular = m v_O. JEE-Adv staple. Derived by differentiating mirror equation. NCERT Example 9.4 (jogger in side mirror) is the entry-level case | mirror_equation, lateral_magnification_mirror, plane_mirror_velocity_image | [T6:relative_velocity_in_optical_systems], [T36:moving_charge_radiation_analogy] |  |
| ↳ differentiate_mirror_eq_to_get_dv_du | nano | ✅ |  | d/dt(1/v + 1/u = 1/f) ⇒ -1/v² dv/dt - 1/u² du/dt = 0 ⇒ dv/dt = -(v²/u²) du/dt = -m² (du/dt) | — | velocity_of_image_in_curved_mirror |  |
| **paraxial_approximation_for_mirrors** | atomic | ✅ |  | All mirror formulas assume rays close to principal axis and small angles (sin θ ≈ tan θ ≈ θ). The justification atomic for f = R/2 and 1/v + 1/u = 1/f. When violated → A11 spherical aberration. EPIC-C STATE_1 wrong belief: "mirror formula works for any aperture" — fails for large-aperture beams | laws_of_reflection, spherical_mirror_geometry, [math:small_angle_approx] | focal_length_f_equals_R_over_2, mirror_equation, spherical_aberration_mirror |  |

## T42 — Refraction Lenses Prism  *(Class 12)*

*26 atomic + 37 nano = 63 concepts.*

| Concept ID | Type | Sim | Diamond | Description (what it teaches) | Requires | Required-by | Targets misconception |
|---|---|:---:|:---:|---|---|---|---|
| **refractive_index_definition** | atomic | ✅ |  | μ = c/v; frequency unchanged across interface; wavelength changes (λ_medium = λ_vacuum/μ). Chain rule μ₁₂ × μ₂₃ × μ₃₁ = 1. EPIC-C STATE_1 wrong belief: "denser optical medium = denser mass" — water > air optically but kerosene < water mass-density yet kerosene > water optically | — | snells_law, apparent_depth_real_depth, critical_angle_TIR, refraction_at_single_spherical_surface, lens_maker_formula, [T44:wave_optics_n_definition] |  |
| ↳ frequency_invariance_across_interface | nano | ✅ |  | f doesn't change at boundary (consequence of boundary continuity). Only λ and v change | — | refractive_index_definition, snells_law |  |
| ↳ refractive_index_table_common_substances | nano | ✅ | 💎 | Water 1.33, crown glass 1.52, dense flint 1.62, diamond 2.42 (NCERT Table 9.1). Just the values | — | refractive_index_definition |  |
| ↳ mu_chain_rule | nano | ✅ |  | μ_AB × μ_BC × μ_CA = 1. Useful for multi-medium problems | — | refractive_index_definition, snells_law |  |
| **snells_law** | atomic | ✅ |  | μ₁ sin i = μ₂ sin r. Denser → rarer: ray bends away from normal. Rarer → denser: bends toward normal. Per RF-G1: own atomic. EPIC-C STATE_1 wrong belief: "ray bends because it 'wants to' minimize path" — actually Fermat's-principle minimization of TIME, not path (the drowning-child analogy in NCERT §9.3 box) | refractive_index_definition, [math:sin_function] | apparent_depth_real_depth, lateral_shift_through_slab, critical_angle_TIR, refraction_at_single_spherical_surface, prism_refraction_geometry, [T44:huygens_derives_snell] |  |
| ↳ bending_direction_rule | nano | ✅ |  | Toward normal (rarer→denser) vs away from normal (denser→rarer). The "memorize-one-case" trick | — | snells_law |  |
| ↳ parallel_emergence_from_parallel_slab | nano | ✅ |  | If both boundaries parallel and same μ on both sides: emergent ray is parallel to incident. Internal angles cancel | — | snells_law, lateral_shift_through_slab |  |
| **apparent_depth_real_depth** | atomic | ✅ |  | μ = real_depth / apparent_depth (for normal-incidence viewing from above). Object appears raised. Multi-medium: total apparent shift = Σ (1 - 1/μ_i) × t_i. EPIC-C STATE_1 wrong belief: "image is at same depth as object" — fishermen learn this empirically | snells_law | lateral_shift_through_slab, [T44:apparent_position_wave_picture] |  |
| ↳ apparent_depth_normal_incidence_assumption | nano | ✅ |  | The μ = real/apparent formula assumes small-angle (normal viewing). Oblique viewing gives more complex shift | — | apparent_depth_real_depth |  |
| ↳ multi_layer_water_oil_apparent_shift | nano | ✅ |  | h_app = h_1/μ_1 + h_2/μ_2. Indian-context: kerosene-on-water layered demos | — | apparent_depth_real_depth |  |
| ↳ fisherman_spear_offset_anchor | nano | ✅ |  | A spear aimed at where a fish APPEARS misses — must aim BELOW. Indian-coastal fisherfolk anecdote anchor | — | apparent_depth_real_depth |  |
| **lateral_shift_through_slab** | atomic | ✅ |  | For a parallel slab of thickness t and μ: lateral_shift = t × (1 - 1/μ) (normal-shift formula via DCP §31.4). Per RF-G1: own atomic. EPIC-C STATE_1 wrong belief: "ray inside slab moves the image" — the displacement is purely a side-shift, image is at same depth-line | snells_law | [T42:silvered_lens_with_slab], [JEE problem-pattern] |  |
| ↳ slab_in_front_of_mirror_normal_shift | nano | ✅ |  | If a slab sits between object and mirror, object appears closer by (1 - 1/μ)t. DCP Example 31.11 | — | lateral_shift_through_slab |  |
| **critical_angle_TIR** | atomic | ✅ |  | sin i_c = 1/μ (going from denser μ to rarer 1). For i > i_c, total internal reflection — NO refracted ray. EPIC-C STATE_1 wrong belief: "some light always transmits" — at TIR, ZERO transmits (idealized). Indian classroom demo: laser pointer in turbid water from below | refractive_index_definition, snells_law | optical_fibre_TIR, mirage_atmospheric_TIR, TIR_prism_periscope_binocular, [T44:goos_haenchen_shift_advanced] |  |
| ↳ critical_angle_values_common_media | nano | ✅ | 💎 | Water 48.75°, crown glass 41.14°, dense flint 37.31°, diamond 24.41°. The "smaller critical angle = more brilliant" insight | — | critical_angle_TIR |  |
| ↳ TIR_must_be_denser_to_rarer | nano | ✅ |  | TIR cannot happen rarer→denser. Common misconception correction | — | critical_angle_TIR |  |
| **optical_fibre_TIR** | atomic | ✅ |  | Core + cladding (n_core > n_cladding); successive TIRs at every wall bounce; >95% transmission over 1km (NCERT). Per RF-G3: own atomic. Indian anchors: BSNL/Reliance Jio fibre rollout in tier-2 cities; medical endoscope (gastroscope) for stomach exam (HCV §18.7) | critical_angle_TIR | [T43:fibre_optic_endoscope], [communications_context] |  |
| ↳ core_cladding_index_relationship | nano | ✅ |  | n_core > n_cladding so light incident at core-cladding boundary exceeds critical angle. Numerical aperture concept | — | optical_fibre_TIR |  |
| ↳ telecommunication_2000_signals_per_fibre | nano | ✅ |  | NCERT: "about 2000 telephone signals" multiplexed per fibre. Indian-telecom rollout anchor | — | optical_fibre_TIR |  |
| **mirage_atmospheric_TIR** | atomic | ✅ |  | Hot road heats air near surface; air layers near ground have lower μ (less dense, hotter); successive refraction bends light upward; at high enough incidence angle → TIR → observer sees inverted "puddle of sky" near road. Per RF-G3: own atomic. Indian-context: every May/June highway between Delhi-Jaipur, Mumbai-Pune | critical_angle_TIR, [meteorology:thermal_gradient] | [T18:thermal_physics_layer_density] |  |
| ↳ superior_mirage_cold_polar_seas | nano | ✅ |  | Inverse case: cold air below, warm above (in seas near poles). Ships appear "floating in sky." Not Indian but worth a callout. | — | mirage_atmospheric_TIR |  |
| **TIR_prism_periscope_binocular** | atomic | ✅ |  | 45°-45°-90° prism with light entering perpendicular to short side: TIR off the hypotenuse, exits perpendicular to other short side. Used to bend light by 90° or 180°, OR to invert an image without flipping (NCERT Fig.9.15 a,b,c). Per RF-G3: own atomic. Indian-context: Indian Army periscope, classroom binoculars, naval submarine periscope | critical_angle_TIR, [T41:laws_of_reflection] | [T43:periscope_design] |  |
| ↳ TIR_prism_better_than_mirror | nano | ✅ |  | TIR has 100% reflection (no silver-tarnish loss). Mirrors lose ~5-10% per bounce; binoculars with 4-6 reflections must use prisms for brightness | — | TIR_prism_periscope_binocular |  |
| **refraction_at_single_spherical_surface** | atomic | ✅ |  | μ₂/v - μ₁/u = (μ₂ - μ₁)/R. Foundation for lens-maker's formula. Derived via paraxial + Snell at the curved interface. Sign convention: incident-light direction positive. EPIC-C STATE_1 wrong belief: "this formula is only for lenses" — it works for any single curved interface (e.g., a glass-rod end, an air-bubble in glass) | refractive_index_definition, snells_law, [T41:cartesian_sign_convention_mirrors] | lens_maker_formula, thin_lens_formula, lens_magnification |  |
| ↳ air_bubble_in_glass_diverges_light | nano | ✅ |  | Glass μ=1.5, air bubble μ=1.0 (lower). Light passing through behaves like a concave (diverging) lens. DCP Example 31.16 + Fig.31.49 | — | refraction_at_single_spherical_surface, lens_combination_in_contact |  |
| **lens_maker_formula** | atomic | ✅ |  | Per RF-G2: own atomic. 1/f = (μ_lens/μ_medium - 1)(1/R₁ - 1/R₂). In air (μ_medium=1): 1/f = (μ-1)(1/R₁ - 1/R₂). DERIVATION question — "what f does this lens have, given material + curvature?" | refraction_at_single_spherical_surface, [math:two_sequential_equations] | thin_lens_formula, lens_magnification, power_of_lens, silvered_lens, [T43:eye_lens_focal_length] |  |
| ↳ sign_of_R1_and_R2_per_convention | nano | ✅ |  | R₁: positive if first surface convex toward incident light. R₂: positive if second surface convex toward outgoing light. The biconvex lens: R₁>0, R₂<0 | — | lens_maker_formula |  |
| ↳ biconvex_R_equal_magnitude_focal_length_R | nano | ✅ |  | For biconvex (R₁=R, R₂=-R) lens with μ=1.5: f = R. Useful "memorize this" result for problems | — | lens_maker_formula |  |
| ↳ lens_in_water_focal_length_4x | nano | ✅ |  | For glass (μ=1.5) lens in water (μ=4/3): f_water = 4 × f_air. (Because μ_g/μ_w - 1 = 1.5/1.33 - 1 = 0.125, vs. μ_g - 1 = 0.5 in air — ratio 4×). DCP Example 31.16 + NCERT Example 9.8(iii) | — | lens_maker_formula |  |
| **thin_lens_formula** | atomic | ✅ |  | Per RF-G2: own atomic. 1/v - 1/u = 1/f. **Note the sign — different from mirror formula (1/v + 1/u = 1/f).** USAGE question — "where is the image, given u + f?" EPIC-C STATE_1 wrong belief: "lens formula is 1/v + 1/u = 1/f like mirrors" — common Class 12 error from over-generalization | refraction_at_single_spherical_surface, lens_maker_formula | lens_magnification, power_of_lens, lens_combination_in_contact, two_lenses_separated_by_distance, lens_image_formation_cases, silvered_lens |  |
| ↳ mirror_vs_lens_sign_difference | nano | ✅ |  | The sign difference traces to incident-light direction: in mirror reflection, light reverses; in lens transmission, light continues. Sign-convention applies the difference cleanly | — | thin_lens_formula, [T41:mirror_equation] |  |
| **lens_magnification** | atomic | ✅ |  | m = v/u (lens) vs m = -v/u (mirror) — see N11.1. For real images: m negative ⇒ inverted; for virtual: m positive ⇒ erect. Same magnitude-interpretation as mirror but opposite sign convention | thin_lens_formula, [T41:lateral_magnification_mirror] | power_of_lens, silvered_lens |  |
| **power_of_lens** | atomic | ✅ |  | P = 1/f (where f in metres). Unit: dioptre (D). Positive for converging (convex), negative for diverging (concave). Indian-context anchor: optometrist's "−1.5 D" or "+2.5 D" spectacle prescription | thin_lens_formula | lens_combination_in_contact, two_lenses_separated_by_distance, [T43:prescription_lens_diopter] |  |
| ↳ dioptre_unit_inverse_metres | nano | ✅ |  | 1 D = 1 m⁻¹. The unit. A lens of f=50cm has P = +2 D. NCERT Example 9.8(i) | — | power_of_lens |  |
| **lens_combination_in_contact** | atomic | ✅ |  | Per RF-G4: own atomic. 1/F = 1/f₁ + 1/f₂ (in contact, d→0). Powers add: P = P₁ + P₂. Used to design achromatic doublets (chromatic-aberration cancellation). NCERT Exercise 9.10 + 9.21 | thin_lens_formula, power_of_lens | two_lenses_separated_by_distance, [T43:achromatic_doublet] |  |
| ↳ three_lens_combination | nano | ✅ |  | 1/F = 1/f₁ + 1/f₂ + 1/f₃ for three lenses in contact. Linear extension | — | lens_combination_in_contact |  |
| **two_lenses_separated_by_distance** | atomic | ✅ |  | Per RF-G4: own atomic. 1/F = 1/f₁ + 1/f₂ - d/(f₁f₂). When d = f₁ + f₂: configuration becomes telescope (zero net power but angular magnification). EPIC-C STATE_1 wrong belief: "separation doesn't matter, only individual powers" — wrong for d > 0 | thin_lens_formula, power_of_lens, lens_combination_in_contact | [T43:telescope_length_f_o_plus_f_e], [T43:compound_microscope_tube_length] |  |
| ↳ telescope_configuration_d_equals_f_o_plus_f_e | nano | ✅ |  | When d = f₁ + f₂, the system has effective f = -f₁f₂/(0) — degenerate, behaves as angular magnifier (telescope). Bridge to T43 instruments | — | two_lenses_separated_by_distance, [T43:astronomical_telescope] |  |
| **lens_image_formation_cases** | atomic | ✅ |  | 6 cases for convex lens: (i) ∞ → F (real, dim, inv); (ii) beyond 2F → between F-2F (real, dim, inv); (iii) at 2F → at 2F (real, same-size, inv); (iv) between F-2F → beyond 2F (real, mag, inv); (v) at F → ∞ (used in collimation); (vi) between O-F → virtual, same-side, erect, mag. Plus 1 concave case (always virtual, erect, diminished). DCP Table 31.1 + Fig.31.39–31.44 canonical | thin_lens_formula, lens_magnification | [T43:microscope_object_at_focal_point] |  |
| **lens_aberrations** | atomic | ✅ |  | Spherical aberration (marginal rays focus shorter f than paraxial — HCV §18.17 + Fig.18.29–18.30) + chromatic aberration (μ varies with λ → red f longer than violet f, HCV Fig.18.33). Coma + astigmatism + curvature + distortion are sub-types. HCV-only. JEE-Adv sleeper. EPIC-C STATE_1 wrong belief: "real lenses are perfect" — every camera lens has multiple elements specifically to cancel aberrations | lens_maker_formula, thin_lens_formula | [T43:apochromatic_combination] |  |
| ↳ achromatic_doublet_crown_flint | nano | ✅ |  | Crown lens (low dispersion) + flint lens (high dispersion) combined in contact: same μ for design wavelength but opposite chromatic-correction. Eyepieces of school microscopes are achromats | — | lens_aberrations, lens_combination_in_contact |  |
| ↳ parabolic_telescope_avoids_spherical | nano | ✅ |  | Big telescopes use parabolic primary mirror instead of spherical lens to avoid both spherical and chromatic aberrations. Indian anchor: 2.34m Cassegrain at Kavalur IIA | — | lens_aberrations, [T41:spherical_aberration_mirror] |  |
| **silvered_lens** | atomic | ✅ |  | DCP-unique. Half-silvered lens behaves like a curved mirror with effective focal length: 1/f_eff = 2/f_lens + 1/f_mirror_back. Ray path: refract — reflect (off silver back) — refract again. JEE-Adv staple. DCP §31.6 Important Point #8 + Fig.31.82 + Example 31.28 | lens_maker_formula, thin_lens_formula, [T41:mirror_equation] | (advanced-JEE problem set) |  |
| **prism_refraction_geometry** | atomic | ✅ |  | δ = (i + e) - A; r₁ + r₂ = A (where A = prism angle). The 4-angle quadrilateral geometry at the prism cross-section. EPIC-C STATE_1 wrong belief: "deviation depends only on prism material" — actually depends on incidence angle i too | snells_law, refractive_index_definition | minimum_deviation, thin_prism_deviation, dispersion_by_prism |  |
| ↳ r1_plus_r2_equals_A | nano | ✅ |  | From the AQNR quadrilateral: ∠A + ∠QNR = 180° (since both Q and R are 90°). And r₁+r₂+∠QNR = 180° from triangle. Hence r₁+r₂ = A | — | prism_refraction_geometry |  |
| **minimum_deviation** | atomic | ✅ |  | At δ_min: i = e, r₁ = r₂ = A/2. Refractive index formula: μ = sin((A + δ_m)/2) / sin(A/2). The standard lab method to measure μ of a prism material in physics-practical class. Indian classroom anchor: every CBSE Class 12 physics-practical | prism_refraction_geometry, snells_law | thin_prism_deviation, dispersion_by_prism |  |
| ↳ delta_vs_i_plot_shape | nano | ✅ |  | δ-vs-i plot is U-shaped with minimum at i=e. Two different i values give same δ (symmetric). NCERT Fig.9.24 | — | minimum_deviation |  |
| **thin_prism_deviation** | atomic | ✅ |  | For small A: δ = (μ - 1) A. Simpler formula, used in achromatic-prism design. Direct-vision spectroscope uses combination of thin prisms with no net deviation but full dispersion | minimum_deviation, [math:sin_small_angle] | dispersion_by_prism, achromatic_combination (achromatic) |  |
| **dispersion_by_prism** | atomic | ✅ |  | μ varies with λ (Table 9.2: crown glass μ_violet=1.533 > μ_red=1.515; flint glass μ_violet=1.663 > μ_red=1.622). Hence δ varies with λ. White light splits into VIBGYOR. Indian-context anchor: every Class 12 physics-practical prism experiment | thin_prism_deviation, prism_refraction_geometry | achromatic_combination, rainbow_formation, [T44:wavelength_dependent_n] |  |
| ↳ newton_recombination_experiment | nano | ✅ |  | Newton's classic: first prism splits → second inverted prism recombines into white. NCERT Fig.9.26 | — | dispersion_by_prism |  |
| ↳ violet_bends_most_red_least_VIBGYOR | nano | ✅ |  | Shorter λ → higher μ → larger δ. Violet bends most, red least. The "VIBGYOR top-to-bottom in rainbow" order | — | dispersion_by_prism |  |
| **achromatic_combination** | atomic | ✅ |  | Two prisms (one crown + one flint) of different angles can combine to produce: (a) deviation without dispersion (achromatic prism — used in periscopes that need to bend light a fixed angle without color-fringing), OR (b) dispersion without deviation (direct-vision spectroscope — used in astronomy to identify Fraunhofer lines without bending the beam). NCERT Exercise 9.23 | thin_prism_deviation, dispersion_by_prism | (binocular eyepiece + camera lens design) |  |
| **rainbow_formation** | atomic | ✅ |  | Per RF-G5: own atomic. Primary rainbow: sunlight refracts into water droplet → internally reflects ONCE → refracts out at 42° to incoming sunlight (red outer, violet inner). Secondary rainbow: TWO internal reflections → 50° angle (red inner, violet outer — REVERSED order). Indian-context anchor: monsoon-rainbow universal experience. NCERT Fig.9.27 (a)+(b)+(c) | dispersion_by_prism, snells_law, critical_angle_TIR | (atmospheric-optics elective) |  |
| ↳ primary_red_outside_secondary_red_inside | nano | ✅ |  | The color-order reversal in secondary rainbow is the diagnostic. If you see only one, it's primary; if both, check which is brighter (primary is) and which has red on top (primary does) | — | rainbow_formation |  |
| ↳ rainbow_requires_sun_behind_observer | nano | ✅ |  | Sun on one side of sky (~western horizon at sunset rainbow), rain on other side. The "back to sun" rule | — | rainbow_formation |  |
| **scattering_rayleigh** | atomic | ✅ | 💎 | Per RF-G5: own atomic. Intensity scattered ∝ 1/λ⁴. Shorter λ (blue, violet) scatter more. Sky appears blue (violet scattered even more but eye less sensitive). Sunset/sunrise red (long path through atmosphere strips blue/violet, leaves red). Indian-context anchor: every Indian evening sky + diamond/peacock-feather iridescence | refractive_index_definition, [T44:wave_intensity_lambda_dependence] | (atmospheric-optics elective) |  |
| ↳ white_clouds_a_greater_than_lambda | nano | ✅ |  | When scatterers (water droplets) are much larger than λ: all wavelengths scatter equally → white. Hence clouds appear white, sky appears blue | — | scattering_rayleigh |  |
| ↳ red_danger_signals_long_wavelength | nano | ✅ |  | NCERT explicit note: red used for traffic signals + ambulance lights because least scattered → reaches farthest. Indian-traffic universal anchor | — | scattering_rayleigh |  |
| **eye_accommodation_defects** | atomic | ✅ |  | Per RF-G6: bundled atomic. Eye lens varies focal length via ciliary muscle (accommodation). Defects: (i) Myopia (near-sighted, f too short) → fix with concave (diverging) lens; (ii) Hypermetropia (far-sighted, f too long) → fix with convex (converging); (iii) Astigmatism (cornea non-spherical) → fix with cylindrical lens; (iv) Presbyopia (age-related accommodation loss) → fix with bifocals. Indian anchors: Lenskart / Titan Eye+ / school eye-camps. NCERT §9.9.1 + Examples 9.10–9.12 | thin_lens_formula, power_of_lens | [T43:spectacle_prescription_optometry] |  |
| ↳ myopic_far_point_finite | nano | ✅ |  | Myopic person's far point is closer than infinity (e.g., 80 cm in NCERT Example 9.11). Required power of corrective lens: P = -1/(far point in m). For 80cm: P = -1.25 D (concave) | — | eye_accommodation_defects |  |
| ↳ hypermetropic_near_point_far | nano | ✅ |  | Hypermetropic person's near point > 25cm (e.g., 75cm in NCERT Example 9.12). For comfortable reading at 25cm: needs +2.67 D (convex). Common in elderly Indians | — | eye_accommodation_defects |  |
| ↳ astigmatism_cornea_non_spherical | nano | ✅ |  | Cornea has different curvature in vertical vs horizontal plane. Vertical lines clear but horizontal blurred (or vice versa). Cylindrical lens with axis aligned correctly compensates | — | eye_accommodation_defects |  |
| ↳ presbyopia_age_related_bifocals | nano | ✅ |  | After ~40 years, ciliary muscle weakens, lens can't deform enough for near vision. Many Indians need both — distance correction + reading correction → bifocal/progressive spectacles | — | eye_accommodation_defects |  |

## T44 — Wave Optics  *(Class 12)*

*27 atomic + 6 nano = 33 concepts.*

| Concept ID | Type | Sim | Diamond | Description (what it teaches) | Requires | Required-by | Targets misconception |
|---|---|:---:|:---:|---|---|---|---|
| **wavefront_types** | atomic | ✅ |  | Plane / spherical / cylindrical wavefronts; locus of in-phase points | — | [`huygens_principle`, `reflection_wave_theory`, `refraction_wave_theory_snells_law`] |  |
| **huygens_principle** | atomic | ✅ |  | Every point on wavefront = source of secondary spherical wavelets; new wavefront = tangent envelope after time τ | [`wavefront_types`] | [`reflection_wave_theory`, `refraction_wave_theory_snells_law`, `single_slit_diffraction_geometry`] |  |
| ↳ backward_wave_problem | nano | minimal |  | Why secondary wavelets don't generate backward wave — historical hand-wave, resolved by Kirchhoff diffraction theory | — | — |  |
| **reflection_wave_theory** | atomic | ✅ |  | Derivation of law of reflection (i = r) using Huygens construction (BC = vτ = AE) | [`huygens_principle`] | — |  |
| **refraction_wave_theory_snells_law** | atomic | ✅ |  | Derivation of n_1 sin i = n_2 sin r using BC = v_1τ and AE = v_2τ; n_2/n_1 = v_1/v_2 | [`huygens_principle`] | [`apparent_depth`, `critical_angle_TIR`, `refractive_index_definition`] |  |
| ↳ wave_speed_changes_freq_does_not | nano | ✅ |  | At a medium boundary, ν stays; λ and v change | — | — |  |
| **doppler_effect_light** | atomic | ✅ |  | Δν/ν = −v_radial/c for v ≪ c; red shift (galaxy receding) vs blue shift (approaching) | [`refraction_wave_theory_snells_law` *(weak)*] | — |  |
| **superposition_principle_waves** | atomic | ✅ |  | Resultant displacement = vector sum of individual displacements at a point | — | [`coherent_vs_incoherent_sources`, `ydse_intensity_distribution`] |  |
| **coherent_vs_incoherent_sources** | atomic | ✅ |  | Coherent = constant phase relationship → stable interference; incoherent = random phase → intensities add (I = 2I₀) | [`superposition_principle_waves`] | [`ydse_setup_geometry`, `ydse_intensity_distribution`] |  |
| ↳ time_average_intensity_2I0 | nano | ✅ |  | When φ rapidly varies, ⟨cos²(φ/2)⟩ = 1/2 → I = 2I₀ | — | — |  |
| **path_difference_phase_difference** | atomic | ✅ |  | Δφ = (2π/λ)·Δx; constructive: Δx = nλ; destructive: Δx = (n+½)λ | [`superposition_principle_waves`] | [`ydse_path_difference_formula`, `single_slit_minima_condition`] |  |
| **ydse_setup_geometry** | atomic | ✅ |  | Two pinholes S₁, S₂ behind master pinhole S; spherical waves interfere on distant screen | [`coherent_vs_incoherent_sources`] | [`ydse_path_difference_formula`, `ydse_fringe_width`, `ydse_intensity_distribution`] |  |
| ↳ thomas_young_locking_phases | nano | ✅ |  | Master pinhole S "locks" phases — any abrupt phase change in S transfers identically to S₁, S₂ | — | — |  |
| **ydse_path_difference_formula** | atomic | ✅ |  | Δx = xd/D for x, d ≪ D (binomial approximation) | [`ydse_setup_geometry`, `path_difference_phase_difference`] | [`ydse_fringe_width`, `ydse_bright_dark_positions`] |  |
| **ydse_fringe_width** | atomic | ✅ |  | β = λD/d (fringe spacing); uniform spacing between consecutive bright OR dark | [`ydse_path_difference_formula`] | [`ydse_with_white_light_central_white`, `ydse_screen_distance_effect`] |  |
| **ydse_bright_dark_positions** | atomic | ✅ |  | Bright at x_n = nλD/d; dark at x_n = (n+½)λD/d | [`ydse_fringe_width`] | — |  |
| **ydse_intensity_distribution** | atomic | ✅ |  | I = 4I₀cos²(φ/2); periodic pattern between 0 and 4I₀ | [`coherent_vs_incoherent_sources`, `ydse_path_difference_formula`] | [`ydse_with_white_light_central_white`] |  |
| **ydse_with_white_light_central_white** | atomic | ✅ |  | Central fringe = white (all λ overlap at Δx = 0); side fringes = coloured (red farthest, then no clear pattern) | [`ydse_fringe_width`, `dispersion_by_prism` *(T42)*] | — |  |
| ↳ s_over_S_less_than_lambda_over_d | nano | ✅ |  | Source-slit condition s/S < λ/d for fringes to be visible | — | — |  |
| **single_slit_diffraction_geometry** | atomic | ✅ |  | Slit width a, screen at distance D, divide into N parallel secondary sources (Huygens); path difference between edges = a sinθ ≈ aθ | [`huygens_principle`, `path_difference_phase_difference`] | [`single_slit_minima_condition`, `fraunhofer_diffraction_circular`, `resolving_power_microscope` *(T43)*, `resolving_power_telescope` *(T43)*] |  |
| **single_slit_minima_condition** | atomic | ✅ |  | Zero intensity at aθ = nλ, n = ±1, ±2, ...; halve-and-cancel argument | [`single_slit_diffraction_geometry`] | [`fraunhofer_diffraction_circular`] |  |
| **single_slit_secondary_maxima** | atomic | ✅ |  | Weaker peaks at aθ = (n+½)λ; intensity drops off rapidly | [`single_slit_minima_condition`] | — |  |
| **central_max_double_width** | atomic | ✅ |  | Central bright fringe = 2λ/a wide; secondary maxima = λ/a wide | [`single_slit_minima_condition`] | — |  |
| **diffraction_vs_interference_distinction** | atomic | ✅ |  | Few sources → "interference"; many sources → "diffraction" (Feynman quote); intensity-redistribution explanation | [`ydse_intensity_distribution`, `single_slit_minima_condition`] | — |  |
| **double_slit_combined_diffraction_envelope** | atomic | ✅ |  | Real YDSE pattern = double-slit cos² × single-slit (sinα/α)² envelope; missing orders when d/a is integer | [`ydse_intensity_distribution`, `single_slit_diffraction_geometry`] | — |  |
| **fraunhofer_diffraction_circular_aperture** | atomic | ✅ |  | Airy pattern: central disk of radius r_0 ≈ 1.22λf/(2a); concentric rings | [`single_slit_diffraction_geometry`] | [`resolving_power_telescope` *(T43)*, `resolving_power_microscope` *(T43)*] |  |
| **fresnel_distance_validity_ray_optics** | atomic | ✅ |  | z_F = a²/λ; beyond z_F diffraction spreading dominates over geometric aperture; ray optics breaks down | [`single_slit_diffraction_geometry`] | — |  |
| **polarisation_transverse_wave_proof** | atomic | ✅ |  | Two-polaroid experiment: rotate analyzer relative to polarizer → intensity varies from full to zero → light is transverse | — | [`malus_law_polariser_analyzer`, `brewsters_law_reflection_polarisation`] |  |
| ↳ string_analogy_for_polarisation | nano | ✅ |  | Slot polariser on long string: only wave parallel to slot passes | — | — |  |
| **malus_law_polariser_analyzer** | atomic | ✅ |  | I = I₀ cos²θ where θ = angle between polariser and analyzer transmission axes | [`polarisation_transverse_wave_proof`] | — |  |
| **polaroid_mechanism_dichroism** | atomic | ✅ |  | Polaroid material absorbs E-vector along one axis, transmits perpendicular axis (selective absorption) | [`polarisation_transverse_wave_proof`] | [`malus_law_polariser_analyzer`] |  |
| **brewsters_law_reflection_polarisation** | atomic | ✅ |  | At Brewster's angle iB where tan iB = n, reflected light is fully polarised perpendicular to plane of incidence | [`refraction_wave_theory_snells_law`, `polarisation_transverse_wave_proof`] | — |  |
| **polarisation_by_scattering** | atomic | ✅ |  | Rayleigh scattering polarises light; explains why sky-blue and why polaroid sunglasses block sky glare | [`scattering_rayleigh` *(T42)*] | — |  |

## T45 — Atomic Spectra  *(Class 12)*

*19 atomic + 5 nano = 24 concepts.*

| Concept ID | Type | Sim | Diamond | Description (what it teaches) | Requires | Required-by | Targets misconception |
|---|---|:---:|:---:|---|---|---|---|
| **emission_line_spectrum** | atomic | ✅ |  | Hot rarefied gas emits at discrete wavelengths only; "fingerprint" of element; appears as bright lines on dark background | [`bohr_third_postulate_transition_photon_emission` *(T47)*] | [`hydrogen_emission_spectrum_overview`, `balmer_series_visible`] |  |
| **absorption_line_spectrum** | atomic | ✅ |  | White light through cool gas → dark lines at same wavelengths as emission; gas absorbs only matching photons | [`emission_line_spectrum`, `bohr_third_postulate_transition_photon_emission` *(T47)*] | — |  |
| ↳ kirchoffs_radiation_law_emission_absorption | nano | minimal |  | A good emitter at a wavelength is also a good absorber at that wavelength | — | — |  |
| **hydrogen_emission_spectrum_overview** | atomic | ✅ |  | H spectrum has 5 visible+UV+IR series: Lyman, Balmer, Paschen, Brackett, Pfund. Each series = transitions to same final n_f | [`emission_line_spectrum`, `energy_level_diagram_hydrogen` *(T47)*] | [`balmer_series_visible`, `lyman_series_uv`, `paschen_series_ir`, `brackett_pfund_series_far_ir`, `rydberg_formula_general`] |  |
| **balmer_series_visible** | atomic | ✅ |  | n_f = 2; 1/λ = R(1/4 − 1/n²) for n = 3, 4, 5...; H_α = 656.3 nm (red), H_β = 486.1 nm (blue-green), H_γ = 434.1 nm (violet); series limit = 364.6 nm | [`hydrogen_emission_spectrum_overview`, `bohr_energy_in_nth_orbit` *(T47)*] | [`rydberg_formula_general`] |  |
| **lyman_series_uv** | atomic | ✅ |  | n_f = 1; transitions n → 1; 1/λ = R(1 − 1/n²); 91.2–121.6 nm; ALL in UV (invisible to eye) | [`hydrogen_emission_spectrum_overview`, `bohr_energy_in_nth_orbit` *(T47)*] | [`rydberg_formula_general`] |  |
| **paschen_series_ir** | atomic | ✅ |  | n_f = 3; transitions n → 3; 820–1875 nm range; ALL in IR | [`hydrogen_emission_spectrum_overview`, `bohr_energy_in_nth_orbit` *(T47)*] | [`rydberg_formula_general`] |  |
| **brackett_pfund_series_far_ir** | atomic | ✅ |  | Brackett: n_f = 4; Pfund: n_f = 5; both far-IR. Formulas analogous | [`hydrogen_emission_spectrum_overview`, `bohr_energy_in_nth_orbit` *(T47)*] | — |  |
| **rydberg_formula_general** | atomic | ✅ |  | 1/λ = RZ²(1/n_f² − 1/n_i²); R = 1.097 × 10⁷ m⁻¹; derived theoretically from Bohr energy formula | [`bohr_energy_in_nth_orbit` *(T47)*, `bohr_third_postulate_transition_photon_emission` *(T47)*, `hydrogen_like_ion_Z_factor` *(T47)*] | [`series_limit_each_series`, `number_of_spectral_lines_combinatorial`, `hydrogen_like_ion_spectrum`] |  |
| ↳ rydberg_constant_theoretical_vs_empirical | nano | ✅ |  | R = me⁴/(8ε₀²h³c); theoretical R = 1.03 × 10⁷ m⁻¹ very close to empirical 1.097 × 10⁷ m⁻¹. **Direct confirmation of Bohr model.** | [`rydberg_formula_general`] | — |  |
| **series_limit_each_series** | atomic | ✅ |  | n_i → ∞: 1/λ_min = R Z²/n_f². Balmer limit = 364.6 nm; Lyman limit = 91.2 nm; Paschen limit = 820 nm | [`rydberg_formula_general`] | — |  |
| **number_of_spectral_lines_combinatorial** | atomic | ✅ |  | From state n_max, atoms can transition to any lower state → total possible lines = n(n−1)/2 | [`rydberg_formula_general`, `energy_level_diagram_hydrogen` *(T47)*] | — |  |
| **hydrogen_like_ion_spectrum** | atomic | ✅ |  | For He⁺ (Z=2), Li²⁺ (Z=3): wavelengths scale as 1/Z². Same Lyman/Balmer/Paschen structure but Z² shorter | [`rydberg_formula_general`, `hydrogen_like_ion_Z_factor` *(T47)*] | — |  |
| **spectral_line_doppler_shift_red_blue** | atomic | ✅ |  | Moving source: λ_observed = λ_emitted (1 ± v/c); receding stars → red shift; approaching → blue shift | [`doppler_effect_light` *(T44)*, `emission_line_spectrum`] | [`hubbles_law_cosmology` *(future)*] |  |
| **x_ray_production_coolidge_tube** | atomic | ✅ |  | Filament + metal target + high voltage (~kV); accelerated electrons strike target; X-rays emerge through Be window | [`em_radiation_from_accelerating_charge`, `kinetic_energy_eV_conversion`] | [`x_ray_continuous_bremsstrahlung_cutoff`, `x_ray_characteristic_k_alpha_k_beta`] |  |
| **x_ray_continuous_bremsstrahlung_cutoff** | atomic | ✅ |  | Decelerating electrons emit continuous-wavelength X-rays; cutoff wavelength λ_min = hc/eV (depends ONLY on accelerating voltage); independent of target material | [`x_ray_production_coolidge_tube`, `photon_energy_hf` *(T46)*] | — |  |
| **x_ray_characteristic_k_alpha_k_beta** | atomic | ✅ |  | Sharp peaks at specific wavelengths characteristic of target material; K_α = transition L→K; K_β = M→K; depends on Z of target | [`x_ray_production_coolidge_tube`, `energy_level_diagram_hydrogen` *(T47)*] | [`moseley_law`] |  |
| **moseley_law** | atomic | ✅ |  | √ν = a(Z − b); X-ray frequency √ proportional to (Z − screening constant); led to ordering elements by Z not atomic mass | [`x_ray_characteristic_k_alpha_k_beta`] | — |  |
| **stimulated_emission_spontaneous_absorption** | atomic | ✅ |  | 3 processes: (a) absorption: photon kicks atom from E₁→E₂; (b) spontaneous: E₂→E₁ random emission (Einstein A); (c) stimulated: photon causes E₂→E₁ emission of identical photon (Einstein B) | [`bohr_third_postulate_transition_photon_emission` *(T47)*] | [`laser_population_inversion_metastable_state`, `he_ne_laser_construction`] |  |
| ↳ einstein_a_and_b_coefficients | nano | minimal |  | Spontaneous emission rate = A₂₁; stimulated rate = B₂₁ · u(ν); detailed balance gives A/B = 8πhν³/c³ | — | — |  |
| **laser_population_inversion_metastable_state** | atomic | ✅ |  | Normally N₂ < N₁ (Boltzmann); need pumping to invert (N₂ > N₁); metastable state (lifetime ~ms not ~ns) accumulates population | [`stimulated_emission_spontaneous_absorption`] | [`he_ne_laser_construction`] |  |
| **he_ne_laser_construction** | atomic | ✅ |  | He (90%) + Ne (10%) gas mixture; He excited by discharge → resonantly pumps Ne to E₂ = 20.66 eV → lasing transition E₂ → E₁ at 632.8 nm (red) | [`laser_population_inversion_metastable_state`] | — |  |
| ↳ laser_properties_coherent_monochromatic_directional | nano | ✅ |  | All photons same wavelength + same phase + same direction; Δλ/λ ~ 10⁻⁶; beam diverges <1 mrad | — | — |  |
| ↳ laser_uses_indian_context | nano | visual |  | Aravind Eye Hospital LASIK + medical surgery + CD/DVD readers + barcode scanners + Indian Army range-finders + fiber-optic communication (BharatNet) | — | — |  |

## T46 — Dual Nature  *(Class 12)*

*18 atomic + 4 nano = 22 concepts.*

| Concept ID | Type | Sim | Diamond | Description (what it teaches) | Requires | Required-by | Targets misconception |
|---|---|:---:|:---:|---|---|---|---|
| **work_function_phi_zero** | atomic | ✅ |  | Min energy required for electron to escape metal surface. φ₀ in eV. Cs lowest (2.14), Pt highest (5.65). Depends on metal + surface | — | [`einstein_photoelectric_equation`, `threshold_frequency_v_zero`, `electron_emission_modes`] |  |
| **electron_emission_modes** | atomic | ✅ |  | 3 ways electrons escape: (i) thermionic (heating), (ii) field emission (~10⁸ V/m), (iii) photoelectric (light) | [`work_function_phi_zero`] | [`photoelectric_effect_phenomenology`] |  |
| **photoelectric_effect_phenomenology** | atomic | ✅ |  | Hertz 1887 + Hallwachs/Lenard 1886-1902: UV light on metal → electron emission → photocurrent. Photosensitive substances. | [`electron_emission_modes`] | [`photocurrent_vs_intensity`, `stopping_potential_v_zero`, `threshold_frequency_v_zero`] |  |
| **photocurrent_vs_intensity_linear** | atomic | ✅ |  | At fixed ν > ν₀ and fixed positive V: photocurrent ∝ intensity (linear). Saturation current = N_photoelectrons/sec | [`photoelectric_effect_phenomenology`] | [`einstein_photoelectric_equation`] |  |
| **photocurrent_vs_voltage_saturation** | atomic | ✅ |  | At fixed ν, fixed intensity: photocurrent saturates at high +V (all photoelectrons collected); reverses to 0 at retarding −V (stopping potential V₀) | [`photocurrent_vs_intensity_linear`] | [`stopping_potential_v_zero`] |  |
| **stopping_potential_v_zero** | atomic | ✅ |  | The minimum negative V₀ at which photocurrent = 0; relates to K_max of most energetic photoelectron via eV₀ = K_max | [`photocurrent_vs_voltage_saturation`] | [`einstein_photoelectric_equation`, `stopping_potential_vs_frequency_linear`] |  |
| ↳ stopping_potential_independent_of_intensity | nano | ✅ |  | For fixed ν, V₀ does NOT depend on intensity — only on frequency + metal | — | — |  |
| **stopping_potential_vs_frequency_linear** | atomic | ✅ |  | V₀ vs ν straight line: slope = h/e (universal), y-intercept = −φ₀/e (metal-specific); below threshold frequency ν₀, no photoemission | [`stopping_potential_v_zero`] | [`einstein_photoelectric_equation`, `threshold_frequency_v_zero`] |  |
| **threshold_frequency_v_zero** | atomic | ✅ |  | ν₀ = φ₀/h; minimum frequency for photoemission. Below ν₀ NO emission no matter how bright the light | [`work_function_phi_zero`] | [`einstein_photoelectric_equation`] |  |
| **photoelectric_emission_instantaneous** | atomic | ✅ |  | Emission starts within ~10⁻⁹ s of light striking surface, even at very dim light. NOT energy-accumulation as wave theory predicts | [`photoelectric_effect_phenomenology`] | [`wave_theory_fails_to_explain_photoelectric`] |  |
| **wave_theory_fails_to_explain_photoelectric** | atomic | ✅ |  | 4 failures: (1) K_max should depend on intensity (doesn't — depends on ν); (2) no ν₀ should exist (does); (3) emission should be slow at dim light (instantaneous); (4) wave can't pump energy into one electron only | [`photocurrent_vs_intensity_linear`, `stopping_potential_independent_of_intensity` *(nano)*, `threshold_frequency_v_zero`, `photoelectric_emission_instantaneous`] | [`einstein_photoelectric_equation`, `photon_particle_nature_of_light`] |  |
| **einstein_photoelectric_equation** | atomic | ✅ |  | K_max = hν − φ₀ = (1/2)mv²_max = eV₀. Each photon = 1 quantum hν; absorbed by 1 electron; explains ALL 4 observations | [`work_function_phi_zero`, `wave_theory_fails_to_explain_photoelectric`, `photon_energy_hf`] | [`photon_particle_nature_of_light`, `milikan_verification_planck_constant`] |  |
| ↳ photoelectric_intensity_increases_count_not_energy | nano | ✅ |  | Higher intensity = more photons/sec → more electrons/sec, but EACH electron still gets hν energy (not more) | — | — |  |
| **photon_particle_nature_of_light** | atomic | ✅ |  | 5 properties: (i) E = hν, (ii) p = hν/c = h/λ, (iii) all photons of given ν have same E, p; intensity = N·E (count, not energy/photon); (iv) electrically neutral; (v) energy+momentum conserved in photon-particle collisions | [`einstein_photoelectric_equation`] | [`de_broglie_wavelength`] |  |
| **milikan_verification_planck_constant** | atomic | ✅ |  | Millikan 1906-1916: measured V₀ vs ν slope for sodium → calculated h. Got h ≈ 6.626 × 10⁻³⁴ J·s, matching Planck. Nobel 1923 | [`stopping_potential_vs_frequency_linear`, `einstein_photoelectric_equation`] | — |  |
| **de_broglie_wavelength_matter_waves** | atomic | ✅ |  | All particles have a wavelength λ = h/p = h/(mv); massive objects → tiny λ (unobservable); electrons → measurable λ ~ X-ray range; **theory by symmetry: if waves are particles, particles must be waves** | [`photon_particle_nature_of_light`] | [`de_broglie_for_accelerated_electron`, `davisson_germer_experiment`, `de_broglie_explains_bohr_postulate` *(T47 link)*] |  |
| **de_broglie_for_accelerated_electron** | atomic | ✅ |  | Electron accelerated through V: K = eV, p = √(2meV), λ = h/√(2meV) = 1.227/√V nm (V in volts). For V = 100 V, λ = 0.123 nm | [`de_broglie_wavelength_matter_waves`, `kinetic_energy_from_potential`] | [`davisson_germer_experiment`] |  |
| **davisson_germer_experiment** | atomic | ✅ |  | 1927: electron gun → Ni crystal → diffraction peaks at θ=50° for V=54 V. Measured λ = 0.165 nm matches de Broglie 0.167 nm. Nobel 1937 (Davisson+Thomson) | [`de_broglie_for_accelerated_electron`, `single_slit_diffraction_geometry` *(T44)*] | — |  |
| ↳ electron_diffraction_extends_to_other_particles | nano | ✅ |  | 1989 double-slit electron interference; 1994 iodine-molecule interference (10⁶× heavier than electron). Wave nature is universal | — | — |  |
| **heisenberg_uncertainty_principle** | atomic | ✅ |  | Δx · Δp ≈ ℏ (or ℏ/2 rigorously). Cannot simultaneously measure position and momentum precisely. Fundamental, not measurement-error | [`de_broglie_wavelength_matter_waves`] | [`bohr_model_limitations` *(T47 link)*] |  |
| ↳ wave_packet_position_momentum_spread | nano | ✅ |  | Localized wave packet → range of wavelengths → range of momenta. Visualizes Δx-Δp tradeoff | — | — |  |
| **photocell_applications** | atomic | ✅ |  | Photoelectric device used in automatic doors, fire alarms, burglar alarms, light meters, traffic counters, motion-picture audio playback | [`photoelectric_effect_phenomenology`] | — |  |

## T47 — Atomic Models  *(Class 12)*

*19 atomic + 5 nano = 24 concepts.*

| Concept ID | Type | Sim | Diamond | Description (what it teaches) | Requires | Required-by | Targets misconception |
|---|---|:---:|:---:|---|---|---|---|
| **thomson_plum_pudding_model** | atomic | ✅ |  | Atom = positive sphere with electrons embedded like seeds in a watermelon (J.J. Thomson 1898) | — | [`rutherford_alpha_scattering_experiment`] |  |
| **rutherford_alpha_scattering_experiment** | atomic | ✅ |  | Geiger-Marsden 1911 gold-foil setup; 5.5 MeV α from ²¹⁴Bi source; ZnS scintillation screen; observation that ~1 in 8000 deflected >90° | [`thomson_plum_pudding_model`, `coulombs_law`] | [`rutherford_nuclear_model`, `distance_of_closest_approach`] |  |
| ↳ alpha_particle_impact_parameter_trajectory | nano | ✅ |  | Trajectory of α depends on impact parameter b: small b → large deflection; large b → small deflection; head-on → 180° rebound | — | [`distance_of_closest_approach`] |  |
| **rutherford_nuclear_model** | atomic | ✅ |  | All positive charge + most of mass concentrated in tiny nucleus (10⁻¹⁵ m); electrons orbit in surrounding empty space (10⁻¹⁰ m atomic radius) | [`rutherford_alpha_scattering_experiment`] | [`rutherford_model_classical_instability_problem`, `bohr_first_postulate_stationary_orbits`] |  |
| ↳ atom_vs_solar_system_analogy_breaks | nano | ✅ |  | NCERT Example 12.1: if atom scaled to solar system, electron would be 100× farther than Earth from Sun | — | — |  |
| **distance_of_closest_approach** | atomic | ✅ |  | d = 2Ze²/(4πε₀K); for 7.7 MeV α + gold (Z=79): d ≈ 3.0 × 10⁻¹⁴ m. Upper bound on nuclear radius. | [`rutherford_alpha_scattering_experiment`, `electric_potential_energy`] | — |  |
| **rutherford_model_classical_instability_problem** | atomic | ✅ |  | Classical EM theory: accelerating electron radiates → spirals into nucleus in ~10⁻⁸ s. Atoms shouldn't exist. | [`rutherford_nuclear_model`, `em_radiation_from_accelerating_charge`] | [`bohr_first_postulate_stationary_orbits`] |  |
| ↳ continuous_spectrum_prediction_failure | nano | ✅ |  | Classical: spiraling electron emits continuous spectrum. Observation: hydrogen emits discrete line spectrum. Disagreement. | — | — |  |
| **bohr_first_postulate_stationary_orbits** | atomic | ✅ |  | Electron revolves in certain stable orbits WITHOUT emitting radiation (defies classical EM); these are "stationary states" | [`rutherford_model_classical_instability_problem`] | [`bohr_second_postulate_angular_momentum_quantization`, `bohr_third_postulate_transition_photon_emission`] |  |
| **bohr_second_postulate_angular_momentum_quantization** | atomic | ✅ |  | L = nh/2π; angular momentum is integer multiple of h/2π; n = principal quantum number | [`bohr_first_postulate_stationary_orbits`, `angular_momentum_definition`] | [`bohr_radius_derivation`, `bohr_velocity_in_nth_orbit`] |  |
| ↳ de_broglie_wave_interpretation | nano | ✅ |  | Standing-wave condition 2πr = nλ + de Broglie λ = h/p gives mvr = nh/2π — Bohr postulate as de Broglie matter-wave standing-wave | [`de_broglie_wavelength`] | — |  |
| **bohr_third_postulate_transition_photon_emission** | atomic | ✅ |  | Electron jumps from higher energy E_i to lower E_f emitting photon of frequency ν: hν = E_i − E_f | [`bohr_first_postulate_stationary_orbits`, `photon_energy_hf`] | [`bohr_energy_in_nth_orbit`, T45 ALL spectra atomics] |  |
| **bohr_radius_derivation** | atomic | ✅ |  | Combining postulate 2 + Coulomb's law: rₙ = (n²/m)(h/2π)²(4πε₀/e²); a₀ = r₁ = 5.29 × 10⁻¹¹ m (Bohr radius); rₙ ∝ n² | [`bohr_second_postulate_angular_momentum_quantization`, `coulombs_law`, `centripetal_force`] | [`bohr_velocity_in_nth_orbit`, `bohr_energy_in_nth_orbit`] |  |
| **bohr_velocity_in_nth_orbit** | atomic | ✅ |  | vₙ = e/√(4πε₀mrₙ) = (1/n)(e²/4πε₀)(1/(h/2π)); v ∝ 1/n; v₁/c ≈ 1/137 (fine structure constant!) | [`bohr_radius_derivation`] | [`bohr_energy_in_nth_orbit`] |  |
| **bohr_energy_in_nth_orbit** | atomic | ✅ |  | Eₙ = K + U = −me⁴/(8ε₀²h²n²) = −13.6/n² eV; ground state E₁ = −13.6 eV | [`bohr_radius_derivation`, `bohr_velocity_in_nth_orbit`, `electric_potential_energy`] | [`energy_level_diagram_hydrogen`, `ionization_energy_hydrogen`, T45 ALL spectra atomics] |  |
| **energy_level_diagram_hydrogen** | atomic | ✅ |  | E₁ = −13.6 eV, E₂ = −3.4 eV, E₃ = −1.51 eV, E₄ = −0.85 eV; levels converge to 0 at n = ∞; visualization | [`bohr_energy_in_nth_orbit`] | [`ionization_energy_hydrogen`, `excitation_energy_excitation_potential`, T45 spectra series atomics] |  |
| **ionization_energy_hydrogen** | atomic | ✅ |  | Energy to take electron from ground state to ∞: 13.6 eV. Ionization potential = 13.6 V. | [`energy_level_diagram_hydrogen`] | — |  |
| **excitation_energy_excitation_potential** | atomic | ✅ |  | Energy to raise atom from ground state to nth excited state. H first excited (n=2): E₂ − E₁ = 10.2 eV; potential = 10.2 V | [`energy_level_diagram_hydrogen`] | [`franck_hertz_experiment_verification`] |  |
| **franck_hertz_experiment_verification** | atomic | ✅ |  | Mercury vapor + variable-energy electron beam; energy absorbed only in discrete jumps (4.9 eV first); emitted at λ = 253 nm. Nobel 1925. | [`excitation_energy_excitation_potential`, `bohr_third_postulate_transition_photon_emission`] | — |  |
| **hydrogen_like_ion_Z_factor** | atomic | ✅ |  | For He⁺, Li²⁺ (one electron, Z protons): rₙ = a₀n²/Z; Eₙ = −13.6 Z²/n² eV; vₙ proportional to Z/n | [`bohr_radius_derivation`, `bohr_energy_in_nth_orbit`] | [T45 hydrogen-like ion spectra] |  |
| **bohr_model_limitations** | atomic | ✅ |  | (1) Only one-electron atoms work; (2) cannot explain fine structure splittings; (3) no intensity predictions; (4) no Zeeman effect; (5) violates uncertainty principle | [`bohr_energy_in_nth_orbit`] | [`orbit_vs_orbital_quantum_mechanics`] |  |
| **sommerfeld_elliptical_orbits_extension** | atomic | ✅ |  | Circular orbits → elliptical (under inverse-square force); same energy formula holds; introduces orbital angular momentum quantum number ℓ | [`bohr_energy_in_nth_orbit`] | [`orbit_vs_orbital_quantum_mechanics`] |  |
| **orbit_vs_orbital_quantum_mechanics** | atomic | ✅ |  | Bohr "orbit" = definite circular path. Quantum mechanics "orbital" = probability cloud ψ(r,t); ψ² is probability density | [`bohr_model_limitations`, `sommerfeld_elliptical_orbits_extension`] | [T46 wave-particle duality, T47-stage-3 quantum-mech atomics] |  |
| ↳ probability_density_psi_squared | nano | ✅ |  | P(r)dr = \|ψ\|² dV; for ground state hydrogen, P(r) peaks at r = a₀ (matches Bohr radius!) | — | — |  |

*19 atomic + 6 nano = 25 concepts.*

| Concept ID | Type | Sim | Diamond | Description (what it teaches) | Requires | Required-by | Targets misconception |
|---|---|:---:|:---:|---|---|---|---|
| **atomic_mass_unit_definition** | atomic | ✅ |  | 1u = (mass of ¹²C atom)/12 = 1.6605 × 10⁻²⁷ kg; m_p = 1.00727 u; m_n = 1.00866 u; m_e = 0.00055 u | — | [`mass_defect_delta_M`, `binding_energy_E_b`] |  |
| **isotopes_isobars_isotones** | atomic | ✅ |  | Isotopes: same Z, different N (¹H, ²H, ³H); Isobars: same A, different Z (³H, ³He); Isotones: same N, different Z (¹⁹⁸Hg, ¹⁹⁷Au) | [`atomic_mass_unit_definition`] | — |  |
| **nuclear_composition_protons_neutrons** | atomic | ✅ |  | Nucleus = Z protons + N neutrons; A = Z + N (mass number); chemical identity from Z (atomic number) | [`atomic_mass_unit_definition`] | [`nuclear_size_R0A1over3`, `binding_energy_E_b`] |  |
| ↳ free_neutron_unstable_inside_stable | nano | ✅ |  | Free neutron decays in ~1000s (β⁻ → proton + e⁻ + ν̄); but stable inside nucleus due to nuclear force | — | [`beta_decay_neutron_proton_transition`] |  |
| **nuclear_size_R0A1over3** | atomic | ✅ |  | R = R₀ A^(1/3) with R₀ = 1.2 fm = 1.2 × 10⁻¹⁵ m. Volume ∝ A. Universal across all nuclei | [`distance_of_closest_approach` *(T47)*, `nuclear_composition_protons_neutrons`] | [`nuclear_density_constant`] |  |
| ↳ nuclear_density_constant | nano | ✅ |  | ρ_nuclear = mass/volume = A·u / [(4/3)π R₀³ A] = constant ≈ 2.3 × 10¹⁷ kg/m³. **Independent of A.** Comparable to neutron star density | — | — |  |
| **mass_energy_equivalence_E_mc2** | atomic | ✅ |  | Einstein 1905: E = mc². 1 u ≡ 931.5 MeV. Energy "stored" in mass; convertible | — | [`mass_defect_delta_M`, `binding_energy_E_b`] |  |
| **mass_defect_delta_M** | atomic | ✅ |  | ΔM = [Z·m_p + (A−Z)·m_n] − M_nucleus. Always positive. The "missing mass" went into binding | [`atomic_mass_unit_definition`, `mass_energy_equivalence_E_mc2`, `nuclear_composition_protons_neutrons`] | [`binding_energy_E_b`] |  |
| **binding_energy_E_b** | atomic | ✅ |  | E_b = ΔM·c². Energy needed to break nucleus into separate nucleons. Measures nuclear stability | [`mass_defect_delta_M`] | [`binding_energy_per_nucleon_curve`] |  |
| **binding_energy_per_nucleon_curve** | atomic | ✅ |  | E_bn = E_b/A. Plot vs A: peaks ~8.75 MeV at A=56 (Fe), drops to ~7.6 MeV at A=238 (U). Light nuclei A<30 + heavy A>170 have lower E_bn | [`binding_energy_E_b`] | [`nuclear_fission_chain_reaction`, `nuclear_fusion_thermonuclear`] |  |
| **nuclear_force_short_range_attractive** | atomic | ✅ |  | Strong, short-range (~few fm), attractive at r > 0.8 fm, repulsive at r < 0.8 fm. Independent of charge (n-p, p-p, n-n all same). Much stronger than EM | [`binding_energy_per_nucleon_curve`] | — |  |
| **radioactivity_3_types_alpha_beta_gamma** | atomic | ✅ |  | Unstable nuclei spontaneously decay via: α (helium nucleus ⁴He), β (electron/positron), γ (high-energy photon) | [`nuclear_composition_protons_neutrons`, `nuclear_force_short_range_attractive`] | [`law_of_radioactive_decay`, `alpha_decay`, `beta_decay_neutron_proton_transition`, `gamma_decay_excited_nucleus`] |  |
| **law_of_radioactive_decay** | atomic | ✅ |  | dN/dt = −λN; N(t) = N₀ e^(−λt). λ = decay constant. Activity R = λN = R₀ e^(−λt) | [`radioactivity_3_types_alpha_beta_gamma`, [`calculus_exponential_decay`](stage-3-math-tools.md)] | [`half_life_T_half`, `mean_life_tau`] |  |
| ↳ activity_unit_becquerel_curie | nano | minimal |  | 1 Bq = 1 decay/sec; 1 Ci = 3.7 × 10¹⁰ Bq (older unit). | — | — |  |
| **half_life_T_half** | atomic | ✅ |  | T_{1/2} = ln2/λ ≈ 0.693/λ. Time for N to halve. After n half-lives, N/N₀ = (1/2)ⁿ | [`law_of_radioactive_decay`] | — |  |
| **mean_life_tau** | atomic | ✅ |  | τ = 1/λ; time at which N drops to N₀/e. T_{1/2} = τ·ln2 ≈ 0.693τ. Distinct from half-life | [`law_of_radioactive_decay`] | — |  |
| **alpha_decay** | atomic | ✅ |  | ᴬZX → ᴬ⁻⁴_{Z−2}Y + ⁴₂He. Mass number drops 4, atomic number drops 2. Q-value = (m_X − m_Y − m_He)c² | [`radioactivity_3_types_alpha_beta_gamma`, `mass_energy_equivalence_E_mc2`] | — |  |
| **beta_decay_neutron_proton_transition** | atomic | ✅ |  | β⁻: n → p + e⁻ + ν̄ (Z→Z+1, A unchanged); β⁺: p → n + e⁺ + ν (Z→Z−1, A unchanged). Neutrino preserves energy-momentum conservation | [`radioactivity_3_types_alpha_beta_gamma`, `free_neutron_unstable_inside_stable` *(nano)*] | — |  |
| **gamma_decay_excited_nucleus** | atomic | ✅ |  | Excited daughter nucleus (after α or β decay) emits γ-photon to reach ground state. Z, A unchanged. Energies hundreds of keV to MeV | [`radioactivity_3_types_alpha_beta_gamma`, `photon_energy_hf` *(T46)*] | — |  |
| **nuclear_fission_chain_reaction** | atomic | ✅ |  | Heavy nucleus (²³⁵U, ²³⁹Pu) absorbs neutron → splits into 2 medium nuclei + 2-3 neutrons + ~200 MeV. Neutrons cause further fissions = chain reaction | [`binding_energy_per_nucleon_curve`, `radioactivity_3_types_alpha_beta_gamma`] | [`nuclear_reactor_principle`] |  |
| **nuclear_reactor_principle** | atomic | ✅ |  | Controlled fission: fuel (²³⁵U) + moderator (D₂O, graphite) slows neutrons + control rods (Cd, B) absorb excess neutrons + coolant extracts heat → drives turbine | [`nuclear_fission_chain_reaction`] | — |  |
| ↳ indian_nuclear_power_program | nano | visual |  | Tarapur 1969 (TAPS) + Kakrapar + Rawatbhata + Kudankulam (Indo-Russian) + Madras Atomic Power Station + Kaiga. ~7-8 GW installed. AERB regulator. BARC Mumbai R&D. | — | — |  |
| **nuclear_fusion_thermonuclear** | atomic | ✅ |  | Light nuclei (²H + ³H → ⁴He + n + 17.6 MeV) fuse at extreme T (~10⁸ K) into heavier nuclei. Releases energy because product has higher E_bn. Sun's energy source | [`binding_energy_per_nucleon_curve`] | — |  |
| ↳ stellar_nucleosynthesis_pp_chain | nano | ✅ |  | Sun: 4 protons → ⁴He + 2e⁺ + 2ν + 26.7 MeV via p-p chain reactions. Source of all sunlight | — | — |  |
| ↳ iter_india_fusion_program | nano | visual |  | India is one of 7 partners in **ITER (Cadarache, France)** — fusion reactor under construction. **IPR Gandhinagar** is India's fusion R&D lead. SST-1 tokamak operational | — | — |  |

## T49 — Semiconductor  *(Class 12)*

*25 atomic + 16 nano = 41 concepts.*

| Concept ID | Type | Sim | Diamond | Description (what it teaches) | Requires | Required-by | Targets misconception |
|---|---|:---:|:---:|---|---|---|---|
| **energy_bands_in_solids** | atomic | ✅ |  | Valence band, conduction band, energy gap in crystalline solids | [bohr_three_postulates, orbit_vs_orbital, pauli_exclusion(MISSING)] | [intrinsic_semiconductor, n_type_semiconductor, p_type_semiconductor, metal_vs_semiconductor_vs_insulator] |  |
| ↳ band_gap_metal | nano | ✅ |  | Overlapping VB/CB → free electrons at 0 K | [energy_bands_in_solids] | [metal_vs_semiconductor_vs_insulator] |  |
| ↳ band_gap_semiconductor | nano | ✅ |  | Eg ≈ 1.1 eV (Si), 0.7 eV (Ge) — thermally bridgeable | [energy_bands_in_solids] | [intrinsic_semiconductor] |  |
| ↳ band_gap_insulator | nano | ✅ |  | Eg > 3 eV — no thermal carriers | [energy_bands_in_solids] | [metal_vs_semiconductor_vs_insulator] |  |
| **metal_vs_semiconductor_vs_insulator** | atomic | ✅ |  | Three-band-diagram side-by-side classification | [energy_bands_in_solids, band_gap_metal, band_gap_semiconductor, band_gap_insulator] | [intrinsic_semiconductor] |  |
| **intrinsic_semiconductor** | atomic | ✅ |  | Pure Si/Ge — electron-hole pair generation, n_e = n_h = n_i | [band_gap_semiconductor, covalent_bonding(MISSING)] | [n_type_semiconductor, p_type_semiconductor, pn_junction_unbiased] |  |
| ↳ hole_concept_nano | nano | ✅ |  | "Hole" = missing electron in covalent bond, behaves as +q carrier | [intrinsic_semiconductor] | [p_type_semiconductor, pn_junction_forward_bias] |  |
| ↳ thermal_generation_recombination | nano | ✅ |  | Pair generation + recombination dynamic equilibrium | [intrinsic_semiconductor] | [pn_junction_unbiased] |  |
| **n_type_semiconductor** | atomic | ✅ |  | Pentavalent dopant (P, As, Sb) → donor level → electron majority | [intrinsic_semiconductor, energy_bands_in_solids] | [pn_junction_unbiased, transistor_npn] |  |
| ↳ donor_level_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Donor energy state just below CB | [n_type_semiconductor] | [pn_junction_unbiased] |  |
| **p_type_semiconductor** | atomic | ✅ |  | Trivalent dopant (B, Al, Ga, In) → acceptor level → hole majority | [intrinsic_semiconductor, hole_concept_nano] | [pn_junction_unbiased, transistor_pnp] |  |
| ↳ acceptor_level_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Acceptor energy state just above VB | [p_type_semiconductor] | [pn_junction_unbiased] |  |
| **mass_action_law_semiconductor** | atomic | ✅ |  | n_e × n_h = n_i² at thermal equilibrium | [n_type_semiconductor, p_type_semiconductor] | [pn_junction_unbiased] |  |
| **pn_junction_unbiased** | atomic | ✅ | 💎 | Depletion region formation, built-in potential V_bi, no external current | [n_type_semiconductor, p_type_semiconductor, mass_action_law_semiconductor] | [pn_junction_forward_bias, pn_junction_reverse_bias, junction_diode_rectifier] |  |
| ↳ depletion_region_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Charged ion-core region devoid of mobile carriers | [pn_junction_unbiased] | [pn_junction_forward_bias, pn_junction_reverse_bias] |  |
| ↳ built_in_potential_nano | nano | ✅ |  | V_bi ≈ 0.3 V (Ge), 0.7 V (Si) | [pn_junction_unbiased] | [pn_junction_forward_bias] |  |
| **pn_junction_forward_bias** | atomic | ✅ |  | p→+, n→−; depletion narrows; majority carriers flow; exponential I-V above V_knee | [pn_junction_unbiased, built_in_potential_nano] | [junction_diode_rectifier, led_atomic, transistor_amplifier_common_emitter] |  |
| **pn_junction_reverse_bias** | atomic | ✅ |  | p→−, n→+; depletion widens; tiny reverse saturation current I_s; breakdown at V_z | [pn_junction_unbiased] | [zener_diode_voltage_regulator, photodiode_atomic, solar_cell_atomic] |  |
| ↳ reverse_saturation_current_nano | nano | — |  | I_s ≈ μA (Ge), nA (Si); temperature-doubles-per-10°C | [pn_junction_reverse_bias] | — |  |

| ↳ half_wave_rectifier_nano | nano | ✅ |  | One diode, 50% utilization, ripple frequency = supply | [junction_diode_rectifier] | — |  |
| ↳ full_wave_bridge_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Four diodes, 100% utilization, ripple frequency = 2× supply | [junction_diode_rectifier] | — |  |
| **zener_diode_voltage_regulator** | atomic | ✅ |  | Reverse-biased Zener at V_z provides constant output across varying input | [pn_junction_reverse_bias, junction_diode_rectifier] | — |  |
| **led_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | Forward-biased direct-bandgap junction emits photons at hν ≈ Eg | [pn_junction_forward_bias, photoelectric_phenomenology, einstein_photoelectric_equation] | — |  |
| **photodiode_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | Reverse-biased junction; incident hν > Eg generates measurable photocurrent | [pn_junction_reverse_bias, photoelectric_phenomenology] | — |  |
| **solar_cell_atomic** | atomic | ✅ |  | Large-area pn junction, no external bias; photogenerated EHP → V_oc + I_sc | [pn_junction_unbiased, photoelectric_phenomenology] | — |  |
| ↳ open_circuit_voltage_nano | nano | — |  | V_oc ≈ 0.5-0.7 V per Si cell | [solar_cell_atomic] | — |  |
| ↳ short_circuit_current_nano | nano | — |  | I_sc proportional to incident intensity | [solar_cell_atomic] | — |  |
| **transistor_npn** | atomic | ✅ | 💎 | NPN BJT: emitter-base forward, base-collector reverse; α and β current gains | [pn_junction_forward_bias, pn_junction_reverse_bias, n_type_semiconductor] | [transistor_amplifier_common_emitter, transistor_as_switch] |  |
| **transistor_pnp** | atomic | ✅ |  | PNP variant; current/voltage signs reverse | [pn_junction_forward_bias, pn_junction_reverse_bias, p_type_semiconductor] | [transistor_amplifier_common_emitter] |  |

| **transistor_input_output_characteristics** | atomic | ✅ |  | I_B-vs-V_BE input curve + I_C-vs-V_CE output curve (CE config) | [transistor_npn, alpha_beta_relationship_nano] | [transistor_amplifier_common_emitter, transistor_as_switch] |  |
| **transistor_amplifier_common_emitter** | atomic | ✅ |  | Active-region operation; A_v = −β × (R_C / r_in); 180° phase inversion | [transistor_input_output_characteristics, pn_junction_forward_bias] | — |  |
| ↳ phase_inversion_nano | nano | ✅ |  | Output 180° out of phase with input — Class 12 board mark | [transistor_amplifier_common_emitter] | — |  |
| **transistor_as_switch** | atomic | ✅ |  | Operating in cutoff (OFF) or saturation (ON) — never linear active | [transistor_input_output_characteristics] | [logic_gate_not, logic_gate_nand] |  |
| **logic_gate_not** | atomic | ✅ |  | NOT: output = NOT input; single transistor inverter | [transistor_as_switch] | [logic_gate_nand, logic_gate_nor] |  |
| **logic_gate_or** | atomic | ✅ |  | OR: output = A + B; truth table 4 rows | [transistor_as_switch] | [logic_gate_nor] |  |
| **logic_gate_and** | atomic | ✅ |  | AND: output = A · B | [transistor_as_switch] | [logic_gate_nand] |  |
| **logic_gate_nand** | atomic | ✅ |  | NAND: output = NOT(A·B); universal gate | [logic_gate_and, logic_gate_not] | — |  |
| **logic_gate_nor** | atomic | ✅ |  | NOR: output = NOT(A+B); universal gate | [logic_gate_or, logic_gate_not] | — |  |
